O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the final word on medical knowledge, with its content and explanations, and with its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise for you, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And for this reason the work of hands is treated in our region and spread throughout all places; it is a difficult science and worthy of study, and there is nothing to delay it except for the small descriptions in books of ancient times that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed up, and the science is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	For it seems to me that I can make this treatise alive again with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of the tools of cauterization, and of other instruments for the work, with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in it must surmount the science of anatomy, as Galenus says, until he knows the structure of the limbs and their shapes and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of nerves and veins and their numbers, and movement and rest of joints, and the place of their emergence.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Iopras says that one must do with the hand what one cannot do with work, and least of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above must be careful so as not to make a mistake and mislead people; therefore, I have repeatedly warned many of those who engage in this science and who abandon themselves to theory without experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut open an abscess on the neck of a woman and cut into the arteries in the neck; for so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he brought a piece of the bladder with him, and he died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen it called out for a treatment, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if he were to treat it, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took in treatment a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant healerguys removed the break above the wound as tightly as possible, and left it so that the wound had no relief, and finished it thus; and he commanded that it should not be loosened; and delayed it thus that the leg became completely frozen and the bones came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I dislocated it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	However, all the ways to cure him had been exhausted or his member, and he could not be cured; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the members were all lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder, which was an abscess that was corrupted and then inflamed by the evil of its own virulence.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when the chancre is purred by melancholy humor, it cannot be cured except by touching it with iron if it is in a good place so that one can completely destroy what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, very careful son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each division of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For as you must keep yourself so that the bad folk may not speak ill of you: if you take your weapons in agreement, and undertake your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are loosed; and leave behind the expected sicknesses of grief health; and bear your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Some of his admonitions are: 'Do not take up with a bad illness, lest you be called a madman.'
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and water-based medicine, and the subsequent chapters are ordered from the bottom up to the top, and of forms of instruments, and of fermness of cauterization, and of all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter concerns the art of cutting and piercing, of suction cups and wounds, of extracting arrows, and similar matters; and it contains the order and forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter concerns the restoration of dislocations and twists, and similar matters; and it contains orders concerning the shape of tools just as they are to be used, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we must remember the work; it is necessary that I give the quality of help and the harm of each kind.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and the most secret answers; and many learned people would speak of it, and agree with what I say; and I am satisfied with a few words, for I shorten my speech.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps everywhere on all kinds of skin, except for one kind of skin: that is to say, on hot-blooded people who have moist matter, and on dry-blooded people who have dry matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together with matter, some devised and said that cautery is great aid; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is of no help in disease caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and must not be cured by hot disease from heat, nor by dryness; and he who said this, who said that cautery makes great aid for hot and dry diseases that come upon men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man with his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, except for that which is tried by the long usage of the cautery, and who knows by experience the diversity of the complexions of men, their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the effects and space of time; of other complexions we have no fear, even if it comes from cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this should agree and fit together with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery works well if it is applied to the cure of secretions, and has greater power than fiery medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member in any way.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fiery medicines come from one member to another in flight, and bring sickness of relief to the affected member; and by chance fire, for its greatness and for the goodness of its substance, does not burn, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And what I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the truth of things; and because I apologize for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that is found in fire, and the quality of the work, as the philosopher says in proving; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they must be made in what season the cauterization should be done, and let them be prayed for.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all seasons, for because the sudden damage that comes through the aid of cauterization; and most especially the cauterization is for necessary pains without delay that cannot wait for the season when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think once, son, as they do so badly; because with the disease that is cured by cauterization there is no return; and it should be thus; but it is not so; for cauterization is nothing more than medicine that moves the complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is better than medicine for the haste of its value, and for the virtue of its work and its nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And that which is possible to achieve is that the disease comes according to the complexion of the patient and its place and virtue; and superfluities are gathered in him through the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cauterization is administered at the place where he has little surplus and moisture, as with cautery for pain, and similar things, and the like pain does not return; but it did happen a little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And few people understand why the cauterizes are called the medicines of medicine, and that is to see; but they do not believe that cauterizes are worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and cauterizes are the medicines of medicine because when we administered ways of cure in no disease and they do not deserve, then let us administer cauterization, and it deserves.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, open well that cauterizes are the medicines of medicine, not because of the intentions of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancient ones said that the tools of gold are more healing than those of iron, and they spoke of the fire only because of the quality of gold and its high essence; and they said that the fire of healing does not cause pus, but this is not true for some people; and the tools of gold are more healing than those of iron, as it has been said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	But if you heat the gold instrument, you will not know when it is hot enough by its color, and it cools down soon; and if you heat it too much, it goes out into the fire, and so there is sufficient impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, because we have made it ready for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I command you this chapter of the law up to the point where the eyes are less heavy to find.
dou cautere olivaire	to cauterize with olive oil
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	to cauterize with olive oil and to treat headaches, pain in the teeth and throat, and many other diseases caused by cold, including paralysis, palsy, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization should be such that the patient is cured by a liquid medicine that cleanses the head, or three or four times, depending on what the virtues and the habit and the patience of the patient allow him to endure; and then wash the head of the patient again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then have him sit with his hands crossed and place his palms on the back of his neck; after that, place the root of your two fingers on the root of his neck between his two hairlines; then let your two hands come together, and if he bleeds, heat the olive-oil cautery, from which comes this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put the fire cautery on the bone, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in returning; then release your hand gradually, and take hold of the bone if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after taking a piece of twine, put cotton in it wet and soft, and put it on the bone, and let it be III days; after putting cotton wet in wax, leave it for as long as the bone is heated; after treating the wound with ointment that is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the elders said that when the wound takes longer to heal, the more it will scar; and for this reason, let us act quickly.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one must keep the fire cautery on the bone for as long as a part of the bone is burned, and then take off what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And serve the other that he should cauterize so much longer upon, and push so hard from the bone as far as I tell you that women put in their furze for this that the humors may come out; and it must be that the wound is kept open a long time; after it must be cured and made secure.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all cases, save that there is fear in some men; and it seems to me that I should let it alone; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness in other members; and moreover when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first sight of cauterizing seems more safe and gentle to me, and thus I use it in assembly for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all parts of the body there is chronic pain that lasts a long time, then the patient must use herbs and pills called "coqises", and cleansing enemas, oils, and poultices; and if one does the fire cautery which we have just mentioned, it will help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's body is of strong constitution, and that it is not too cold; then apply the fire cautery as we have described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the fire cautery to each horn of the head as we have described above and making the vessel in which the fire is placed; then place the cupping glasses; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels too much pain during this cauterization, I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the corn cauterizations be thinner than those with which we cauterize the skin of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	The fire cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain spreads throughout the head and continues up to the oil, and the chiés is purged with medicine that removes fever, and other cures as I mentioned in the division of diseases, then perform fire cautery according to two methods, that is, with medicinal water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery: Take a sweet alizarin, and peel it off the skin and dip it into the oil of the chiés, then apply it to the temple or place where the pain is with your hand in such a way that you can hold the alizarin on the skin; and when it has been held there for twelve or thirteen hours, then take it off and dip it in garlic juice, and leave the wound for two or three days; then cover it with cotton dipped in wool grease until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of wound care as long as it is healthy; and if you see that this one of some burning medicines that I have written or half-time medicine burner.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "close" for the head is made in the form of a clo or it has I pit of corbeure, and in the middle to a small appearance; and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little slightly, until the halfway of the scar burns; and remove your hand that the artery does not burn, which is gone away, and runs abundant blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in the shape of a string, and place it on the spot for III days; then I put wet cotton in butter, and then cure the spot of wound care as long as it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer which is called "cultellare", at all points, and keep yourself from covering the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	As for the treatment of migraine, as we have already said in the division of diseases, and do not benefit from it, and see that the fire cautery before mentioned in medicine and iron does not satisfy him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and sign so on the sore spot a line half an inch long, and hold your hand back once, and pull it off so that you do not cover the artery and do not come to the bone; and guard against the jaw that moves when you chew, and let the rest of the work lie; but I will tell you how to stop the pain when the artery is copped, and I will show you at what place it happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice to the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him at the nape of the neck as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said, or the extractive chapastre with the cautery having II blades; and this cauterization is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears from cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold, and one has applied liquid medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not cease, then apply this cauterization, which is called "poins", whose form is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After having pierced all around the ear that is troubled, or around both of them since the pain persists at the entrance to the canal, and you have located the place where you want to pierce, and there are X points around each ear; after having done this, cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	that should be cured by fire is not stronger than those that move with fluid, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and do not make any fire for similar things that come from scabs and meat lice.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this kind of torture that moves with fluid from the head and gargling, and it does not matter, then you must treat the disease with three fire tortures: one at the root of the ear, another a little further up the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; apply the fire to the healthy part, and let the half-burned fire remain; and this is the form of the fire torture:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance of the surgical knife that we have put before you is a little more subtle, and it is necessary that the knife be a little thicker; after treatment, keep it as I have said, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexies are old and you treat them as we have said, they do not benefit, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I cut the head, and I put fire to it which is called "vasels," as we have said before, and a cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of tar
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	This is a treatment for this disease: give the patient many large pills that are dry and pungent for the brain; after healing all his head, put on his occiput the resin of saffron, which is written or spoken about in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is well here, it is good; and if not, he does three fire cauterizes on the head at the root, with two spaces between each cauterize; and cure it like the others, and if you see them quiver, and the patient suffers, do one in the middle; and if there is a trade, there are two others on the two horns, and cure him until he is well; and let the cauterizes that are called 'olive' be done as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be washed and clean and that what we have said before be done again; after washing the head of the patient, then he does a fire cauterize on the head and on each of the two horns, one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers and is ill, do three cauterizes on the spine of the back; and let it be until the fire of the last cauterize has gone out, and raise your hand; after that, cure him until he is well, and let the cauterizes that are called 'olive' be done as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For the fire cautery, it is only appropriate for those who are flematic; first, however, the brain must be washed out and other remedies mentioned in the section on great and suffering patients should be used.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot bear the fire, let them gargle and chew to wash out the brain frequently with good meat; afterwards, place the head in the middle and apply the fire according to what we have said before, and also on the neck and each horn; and if the patient is outside and suffering, do so as I have said for those who are paralyzed and have a softening of the spine and neck, applying the fire olive-wise as I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform the following procedure for them:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are excess fluids or corrupted moisture and gross pus, then half-fire cautery as we have said to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy there is excess fluid declining to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he should drink something that clears the brain, according to what has been said in the division before this.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have reposed the head of the patient; after that make a well-formed turban out of linen, also as a circle, if you put it on the head; and let the patient sit with his back well supported and held in place; then present the liniment, and wet it with old butter; and heat it gently by the fire so that he can tolerate it; after that empty the circle from inside the turban and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with another good treatment, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you see cauterization, make many punctures all over the cauterized area.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterizing moistens the scalp, increased; and then put cotton wet in butter and Linseed oil on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes of the hairs
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first the eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient purifying thing, and ward off all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that he orders him to re-apply the scalp, and makes a fire cautery on the scalp, and does two cauterizations on the temples because they are exposed; and keep the cauterization long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the escape of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with mud as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and with caution how to stop bleeding; and never is cauterization done or the bone is removed from behind.
dou cors des larmes	the tears of two hearts
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	the tears of two hearts are old and accustomed and are along the veins, or cut off the arteries that are in appearance at the top of the head; and one can see that it is of the cold and wet superfluity, therefore do I make the fire cautery that I said at the beginning of the awing down to the hair: I cauterize the top, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries where haters are removed from the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes well over the brow with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the tears of two hearts flow inside the hair
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give him three cups of ale for three nights; after that he raises his head, and makes a cautery in the middle of the cautery olive; and make two cauteries in the cautery called "clavilis" on the two horns, a little away from the hair; and guard the artery so you don't cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	This is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	So that this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you make two cauteries on the two horns as long as the horns are; and do not let your hand rest until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Oil-colored hair.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has passed that the hair of the oiled have been converted to the parched, and touch oil, and there is done on two ways of cauterization: namely, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are equal, then place the patient in your care; after that, sign on the paper of the eyes a figure that is also as the flesh of the heart, and this is the beginning of the sign to scratch the hairs; then put cotton wet in wax and muskellunge of peony on the oil, then heat the cautery so that this is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize on the figure that you have sewed little by little several times, so that the burn is in the right place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up to the point where the oil comes out; then gently lift your hand, and leave it like that for III days, then put cotton wet in butter as long as the scabs are laid; after the cure of the wound until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that come the hairs, and the paper is softened then start again the cautery on the same middle level, as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper returns to its natural position, and is even, and does not stick to the hair oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal hot cautery is that you command the sick person to leave the hairs as long and even as possible; then make of parchment the shape of the bay leaf; then take French soap and very hot water, each a .Z., and grind them together well; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool down, then pour it on the paper; and if the illness is in only one oil, then put the other also, and cover with cotton wet in oil; and the sick person's joints should be in your hand, and place your thumb over the medicine, and press a little and rub every time the sick person feels tingling from the medicine, for he feels tingling also as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	As you have done for so long, if the medicine has gone to your head.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the medication has passed, if the swelling has gone down, then lift up the bandage as if it were lifted by fire or by incision; and if so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then put more medicine on the swelling where the medicine has gone, until your hairs are long and even, and your nails are cut; and then put cotton wet with oil on it as soon as the feverishness is gone, after treating the swelling which is called 'dysmencorhood' and other things, until it is well.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to bandage yourself well on your wound by great care so that the medicine does not go into your hairs.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the bandage becomes soft, and the hairs become stuck in the oil, then begin again the medicine on that same place which has been softened by the bandage properly, as you have done before; after treating until it is well; and this is the form of the salve of mirth:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to their nature; and do not return the right path to him whose task is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then it is appropriate that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dip the surgeon's knife in a bottle of oil or wine juice as described above; then heat the cauterizer, and place it on the head as if it were the shape of a feather; together with the knife, so that when you see one, it is pointed at the other, and when you do not see it, it is like a tent; but whatever the case, let it be close to your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, let it open and apply the poultice, and dry it out; and if it is closed, re-open it and treat it firmly; after that, place a very hot cauterizer on it, and keep your hand away from the cauterizer over the part under the oil, so that your hands do not go crazy; and put the cauterizer in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the cauterization just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, start the cauterization again, and if you need to do it more often, leave it for III days; after that, put cotton wet in oil on it, and let the dressing dry out until it is well, and if forty days pass and it is still not well, then put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what came in the chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way to cauterize a fistula that no ancient said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	In the case of a fistula, and then cut it; then put in the fissure an extremely small hammer so that this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I make it with the quantity of half an ounce of melting; and hold your hand firmly, so that the patient does not move at all, that the melted mass does not run to his oil; and it is good that you put cotton wet in alcohol or vinegar on the oil: The melted mass, if so artfully applied to the place of the fistula, and will be cured by a marvelous cure.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is cured with the cauterization that we have said, it is good.

de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat

dou movement des dens	the movement of teeth

When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the sick person in your hand; after heat the cautery so that its form comes out in this way that you put a string on the tooth; and place the cautery inside, hot as it is, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then release your hand and continue with the cautery according to your will; after fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and wash it thoroughly.

de la dolor des dens	the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is coldness or heat, and medicines do not help, then there is a need for two types of cauterization: caustice with butter and fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent. Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire if it is such that you squeeze a metal rod or iron bar, and make it thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick person; then heat the cautery, for the form will come later, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand as long as the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will increase on the third day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then he should drink it; and this is the form of the cautery.
