Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	de l'issue de l'huile
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the unraveling of a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the unraveling of woven fabric brings about its disintegration, which can be seen as threads break and become visible; therefore, when you see it covered over, treat it like a wound by stitching it with needles in a circular pattern, double knotting the thread at each end, and wrapping it with wet linen, oil included, until the wound heals; and never restrict the wound with fabric circles,
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs have a good appearance, if it pricks them with the fine needle that comes perfectly from the oil, and chases away the moist albugineous blood and removes the hairs, and cuts them off soon; then extract them so that they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bowels of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is nothing but a bowel that is gathered in oil, resembling water descending, and yet it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the Ovaire is such that you sit the patient on II seats appariled and upright, then take the chief between your hands from both sides, and let the bowels come up to your hairs; then lay them down firmly, and do not descend or move them, and see how the patient's condition changes as if it were alone; and know that if it does not descend, it is water, and the descent of the bowel is not apparilled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you are sitting the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatumile and strike on the horny membrane with the continuation of the conjunctive with the horny membrane and the crown, until the bow is out; and when it is discharged, pour into hot oil mixed with honey, or sharp water or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then is cured from another cure as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	hot oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the appearance of blades in division, and what is necessary to pierce; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands, away from light for the sun, and hold the healthy oil very tightly; then place the paper of oil in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if the eyes are on the right; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; and place the point of the instrument over the crown by its thickness to a rait in that blenchor of oil at the part of the smaller larmier, then bottle the instrument called "almagda" well, and turn your hand around until it pierces into the blenchor of oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the parfont of the measure of the space which is from the prunele jusc’a the end of the noirour; and this is the crown of oil; then you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horny membrane, and then place the instrument at the level where the water is, then express one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now given water, if he looks forward and sees the instrument in his own oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a short while, and if he is given water again in the second vessel, push with the instrument and when it is firmly set and no longer moves, gently remove the magma by turning your hand back and forth; and then put a little gem-water in it again, and leave it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on the other side the oil or else wet linen in oil and with a lot of salt, and bind with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	And, and those from our own land, let us put on common broie with a lot of salt.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the magma cannot enter the oil because of its hardness, for there are some men who have too thick hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so then, separate the conjunctive sine, and don't go too far with it, but make it thin, then pour in the almagest, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient the bed coming forward, where he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and let him be free from all movement, and eat light meats, and do not move his head to the right or left, and let him be tied according to his disposition until three days; then remove it in that very same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put him back in the tie until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate that you do this at the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is appropriate that you adapt it, for because of it the water rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the abscesses come out, so that you pour oil before the seventh day, and apply it with a liquid that softens an abscess; and when it has calmed down, if you take off the veil and put it on his face, so that it covers any day, and stays in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then from the house slowly and slowly, and make himself comfortable there; and know that no servants should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Land of Yak, who told us that in our country a certain medicine is made which sucks up the water, but I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in books of the ancient ones; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the appearances of the shapes of almagda, so that he who does not know them sees them; and let them be of earth properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle substance be in three angles acute behind.
de la char sor le neis	of the neck over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No times are born or are raised various chards that seem scorpions at the mouth of the stone; and if there are such ones or not it has a characteristic charcoal, and if has a good-colored sorrel.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chards which is sorrel and not encrusted, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands toward the sun; and operate his nostrils, and pour the liquid on those chards, and scrub them hard; because what you can support on the spatumile subtil agut from one side, as long as you know that this char is all boney.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, if you open it with the subtile and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if he comes up again or an abscess, as it should, and if it is malignant, then hasten and cauterize it as much as the wound is clean and bone has grown out of all the chards, then pour or pour easily and quickly or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he is still unconscious, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; and if moisture does not go down as it should, know that there is no room in the bone above, for the instrument does not come to cut: therefore you must put a thin thread of linen, and tie it tightly with your hands, and place between each knot or less; and make the patient bite on the string at his power, and pull on the odorant until it comes out through his nose into the mouth; and many times do this to the child for school, and this is a light thing for him who does it; then hold the top that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other top that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know one after another as we are doing with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make the poultice as long as you know that the new has corrupted this cloth, then treat the wound, wash the blood, and dip the cloth in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the wound immediately; make three or more days, as long as the ointments corrode all those who are delayed by the cloth; and then put a stone of plunk in some water for several days until he is well, and if there is need for medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, from which they distil oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Be of silver or gold, resembling a lamp open, as a ring, and bring it also; and if you see it, make a closed ring, and be the instrument flat to purify the head; and I have many times on the head to keep it when they heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the horse's shoulder
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the shoulder neck is a disease that is called "telul", and grows and becomes very large, so much so that it can be seen with the eye; and because of this, you must cut it at the beginning, and burn the bone, then apply fire to the injury; and if you wait too long, and it becomes hard, take care that it does not change color, and has poor sensation: if not, do not touch it with iron, for it is a swollen abscess, because when it is cut, much harm is done to the patient; and the abscess is touched gently, not with fire, and you can cut all of it, if you vacuum the patient and cut without fear, and cure with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and cured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	That is to say when solutions of continued duration come upon one of these jointed parts, it provides little benefit unless in certain men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	For if there is any of this upon anyone, so regard it that the wound is fresh throughout all its length; and then join the two lips together at a seam, then heal it as long as it remains sound; and if the lips are torn on one side or the other, then you must peel off all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then join the two lips together at a seam, and press them down, and powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and incense burned; and put over the powders a piece of plaster of strength or any other plaster at hand, and let it remain there as long as it oozes, then cure it with ointment until it is sound.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of joining thus: you put together with needles as I have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	of the lips with a strong hand inside the lips, resembling grains of sand, smaller and larger ones; then it is necessary that you spread the lips, cut each one individually, and take it with pincers and cut it into parts; then employ the leech after cutting the vitriol, as long as the blood has stopped flowing; and then clean them of the leech, and cure the part from dry things until they are healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	many times on the gums with a hard paste that the old man called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, and let the blood run or the blood flow; then put on the leech vitriol or other restraining and drying powders; and if this gum returns after the incision, and many times again, if it is cut a second time, and cauterized: if it does not return again after cauterization; and these are the shapes of tools to plug.
des sordens	of the orde
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	of the teeth
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure a tooth that hurts to wait to pull it out as long as possible because this is not done without reason; for it is a very high substance until there is no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And so when the disease is constrained by the treament, it is necessary that you are certain with the tooth pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Sometimes the pain leaves the disease, and one thinks that it is the healthy tooth, and has the tooth pulled; nevertheless, the pain does not go away because of this, until we have tried to do this to these patients; and when you are certain about the tooth pain, then you scratch the tooth with a hard twig towards the gum from all sides; then he moves it with your hands or small pliers at one time and one time, as long as they are well loosened, then he tightens the pliers well; and let the head of the shoulder be in your healthy between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After pulling the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out, then take any of these instruments and knock it in from all sides lightly, and move it so as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if his jaw is tight and stuck, then fill it with gauze where the obstruction is; and if he holds it firmly with pliers so that it does not break when extracted; and it is necessary to clean thoroughly under the gum so as to pull out the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must take care that you do not break it, and there remains a part of it, and returns to the patient by the evil of the root with greater pains than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must take care not to do so as do the ignorant doctor who, through his haste and audacity, often breaks any vehicle, and does not administer what we have described; but brings about any evil by the bad roots that they delay or by the broken carriage, as we have often seen it happen; and when the jaw is pulled out, wash the hole with wine or mint and rope; and let them run away without causing pain to come again, which often happens if you employ the hole of vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they do not get stuck in the first place, should be long and thick at the tips, so that they do not double up when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large members so that they do not bend when pulled, and they should be well made of iron, and they should be toothed so that they hold fast.
de la racine des dens	the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root is wet when pulled, you should put cotton moistened with oil on the place or apply it with your finger.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the roots are smooth, because then the pliers that are called 'grinders' do not seem to bite; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you should uncover the tooth entirely around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'alethi', that is to say file, this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and heavy so that it does not break, and the root jumps from it, this is good; if not, then help with all the tools, from which the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument that has two rains, from which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the Rasion of the Dens, and this instrument which seems like a big pliers, whose is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and this instrument is strong so that it cannot break, and know that many tools of dens are; and also other tools that are not accounted for; and the wise masters subtilely choose their tool themselves according to what his work and the disease show him, because there are many diseases where the old man does not teach a tool for the variety of them; and if it does not break the carriage or other bones, on which he lies, if he seeks the tools that fit him, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well held to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove; and then return him his place with medicines appropriate for him, and if he has a cavity in the bone, and it is small, then remove all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in line with the natural shape of the jaw, and the form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the root is between the teeth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be sewn or filed; then cut off the tooth; and if it is attached to the root, take this instrument whose form is like a small pick, and which is made of iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits and fits hard on the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file with a file such as this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime that we make needles; and in lime a tooth pokes and pokes with his hands lightly every day so that it does not move until it chokes; then in the end there is no grinder to all, and its density is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to sharpen the bluntness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth moves and pokes with his hands lightly every day
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth move and poke with his hands lightly every day, so that the patient cannot press on what he bites until he chokes, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and this does not work; then you should restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and rusts, but gold never moves; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you notice any pain on one side, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the hooks between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you can clean it thoroughly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start again at the point where you started, and gently and thoroughly tighten your hand, so that it does not move. And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the shoulders of the wire to a pair of pliers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy tooth and set them so that they do not cut the tongue; and then leave them in this tight position as long as it can be held, and if they slip or run out, if restrained by another wire; if it remains and serves thus all its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the appearance of the attachment of the II healthy teeth and the II molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then if the loose tooth is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not skilled and suffering should meddle with it, and never make the shape of a tooth of a cow's skull, and put it back in its place where it is missing, and hold it as we have said, and remain and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ring of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is lost for the ring of the tongue that comes from nature, which must be so; or by accident of a sore swelling; and the ovraiges are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and put your head in his throat, and lift the tongue; then cope the nervous ligament of the broad, as much as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or not, and it is a sudden sore swelling, so he cuts the ligament and cope the broad ligament; and be careful that the cut is not too perfect, for the artery that is behind; and when you have done so, let the patient drink a little rose or cold water, then put a piece of linen on the tongue; and wash it every night, so that the ligature cannot hold.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood fever comes, then put the vitriol on top of it; and if it does not go away, then cauterize it with a slow cautery, which is good for it; then heal other cures until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark or black or hard color on it, then the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, because it is leprosy; and if it declines to yellow, and there is moisture, then pour the vinegar, and make it with a thin blade, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if it does not go away to your aid, then put the vitriol on top of it until it is burned, and then return to your aid as long as you pull it all out; then lift its head up and down, and heal other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Of the throat come forth from within called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres", and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, if take care: it is an abscess of small size and a little color, so do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for its pain or because it could burst; but let it be until it has gone away, and then take it off, or else it would burst by itself; and if it is of a pale color, and the root is thin, you should prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check that the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the patient in front of the sun, and let his shoulders be in your shade, and the ovary is at the mouth and between his hands, and press the tongue to all the instrument, so that it is this form; and be of silver or gold as well as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And then you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the blade and put it in amber, and raise it further than you can; and do not tie anything with it, then put the bandage on the instrument, so here is the form, which seems a strong one; and yet their heads are curved, and one head is above another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or anvil:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the cope with pliers, so here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be careful not to cut one edge at all, and when you have coped one of the amber, do the same to the other in the same way, and after the incision gargarees the sick with hot water, and easily and quickly, and if there is a little blood coming out, gargaree it with water or cooked pomegranates, or leaves of mirth, and similar things until the wound is healed; then heal him as long as he is well; and never cut in the throat other abscesses than the two ambers, if you cut them like the two ambers.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was lodged in her throat, namely a small-sized abscess; and I had it tightly sealed up all around her throat so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was blocked, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had waited another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had risen two inches from her throat by way of the two small openings from which it discharged.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly pulled out some of the hair with my hand, and it grew back again, and then I cut off another piece, and then I pulled out more hair, and then I cauterized it in her throat: so she stopped growing larger; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the tear descends from the eye, and it is escaped and distant, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is big and round, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the hoof of the abscess is soft, and it is slim, then you should chop it; and that which is round and assembled and is not distant; and it is bloody or of a brown color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its blubber and distance, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument of which we have spoken above; then insert the awl into the eye, and twist it, and chop it with two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; because if you do so much, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has a fear of covering, then you should use fire to cauterize the pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of fire cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your hand, and then press the tongue of the instrument that we have said or fire cautery, and confound with sharp water so that it is not too thick or too clear; and by employing the shape of this instrument, of which I speak here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place a lock of hair on the patient's forehead, as if it were a ring, and dip the instrument that we have spoken of or fire cautery in the medicine, and confound it with sharp water so that it is not too thick or too thin; and by using the shape of this instrument, of which I speak here: Take a lock of hair, as if it were a ring, and dip the instrument in the medicine, and press all the medicine on the lock, so that the patient lies on his side, so that saliva and spittle run out of his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat, and bleeds; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the lock for half an hour, until you see it become dull and the medicine's marks fade; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and dip the instrument in all the cotton on the cord, so that the cotton is wet with the medicine; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and rinse after III or V days or more as needed. And if you need to renew the medicine, dip the instrument again in the medicine, and after the cautery rinse it out with sharp cold water, and cure by gargling until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, save the cautery. If it is cured by fumigation according to this way, take calamus and hyssop and oreganum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put all of them or any of them in a pot, and put it there easily, and make it boil; and the pot can be well glued with strong earth, and put the instrument above it according to this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is of silver or of gold, and let one of the shoulders be put in the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises to the vein through the tube, until the vein is dead; then often begin again, until the vein dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the coming of the abscess, for many things have happened; and do not make this except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog's teeth and put them in the mouth of the sick person so that his mouth does not get too hot; for the dog's teeth do not make the vapor of the wound be very hot in the mouth, and it is good treatment together and salutary.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often times a bone or hair comes out of the mouth, or nothing at all. So you must take what you can see, and press it against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the thing; and if what is not opening up for you and remains in the throat, it is necessary to make the sick person vomit so that his food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps he will spit it up; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and you tie the sponge to it, and then drink it up; and when it comes to the right place, if it comes out hard, then pull hard; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of plunger according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.
de la sansue de la gorge	to take care not to touch the epiglottis, which might prevent the instrument from entering; and do not push the bone inside; and rather let the patient suck on the instrument, so that it may relieve his pain or discomfort; if the patient swallows, or he draws the instrument out whole, evenly
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	do not use the medicine of the throat, as I said in the division, for the treatment of medicines; and when it does not benefit, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, because you press the language to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, whether it is due to a small prick or to tiny claws.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if he doesn't respond, then take a stick and pour it in the throat of the sick person, then pour or blow on the stick with fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is bleeding all the time.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full jug of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it down, and move it with his hand often; and if soon after drinking the water feels the blood, then throw it up.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't vomit as we have said, then suffocate the sick person with ash of the herb called asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the nose; do this many times, for it will help to prevent vomiting.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.
