des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the scorching or fever enters into the bladder, or putrefaction is present therein, and you see that there are water and medicines, so do with all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and this is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three apertures: one on one side, and another on the other, as you see; and let the head of the instrument be such that the medicine which is to be injected stops well in the bladder without any addition, so that the moisture can be withdrawn, and put when necessary; and when you inject your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the syringe in the moisture, and draw while pulling it; if you draw the moisture into the syringe, and then push it with force back into the bladder; if it will enter the moisture into the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the shape of the delicate clyster with which they clisterize the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d'un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenantment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n'as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d'oile et de moistor et d'aigue, et le lie en l'estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken about the ways of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between a stone stuck in the bladder and in the member, and as to what size a stone should be, and about the bladder and penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is stuck in the bladder often comes out with children, and this is a sign that the liquid in the bladder seems to be like water in its subtlety; and I open it, and massage the patient's penis, and turn it many times, and then it gets tighter; and the foundations are melted; and the recovery from this jump is lighter in children up to the age of four, and it is much heavier in old people, and it is moderate between teenage and elderly; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, if it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the waste matter which is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For he never wants to try cutting into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take hold of the patient by the feet, and pull him upside down and move him to the place where the stone is located at the bottom of the bladder, and never cut into it from above; then make him sit between your hands, and his legs be also drawn back so that the bladder hangs down; then feel inside; if you can feel the stone in the space, then quickly cut into it on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out when you touch it all over, then wet your little finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old and infirm, or use your right hand; and press at the bottom, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, feel for the neck of the bladder; then squeeze gently, and push down on the spot where you feel it.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and he commands that he extends to his right hand the sacs above, and with his left hand he holds the skin which is behind the sacs in the part where the waist is made; then I pour the spatumil, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And open between what is between the sacs and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left waist; and let it be right on top of the stone, and your two sides are joined to the foundation, and let the cut be through the navel so that it is wide from the outside, and tight inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps the press if that which is at the foundation, that she should go without work; and know that there is a piece of stone where there are angles and edges: this is difficult to remove; and if part of it is smooth, resembling a ring, and round, its exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A cell so choose where there are angles and margins, make the size larger; and if it does not [break], so that you can extract with tweezers which are also like a file on the head, to move the stone so that it does not escape; or you squeeze with your fingers a fine corbied instrument on the head; and if you can not catch it so, so it is wide a small hole, and if it is peeled, so extract the vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first squeeze the largest at the neck of the bladder, then continue, then move strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, so that it is convenient to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: he dies, or his urine comes again quickly because his veins cannot hold it; but nevertheless you push to extract, or to tear with tweezers, until you extract it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, if you employ the encensement with balm and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and put on top a wet drape with oil and wine, or with oil and rose water and cold water to calm the abscess; then cut off the patient's hair from his neck, and do not untie the bond until three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, if there is a lot of oil and water, then treat with unguentum de finigo and unguentum basilicum until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come out in the wound and corrosion, and frosts of blood in the bladder, and is held back by urine, which is conveyed in a certain way so that it does not jump with urine: then you must put your hand in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and pour it out; then raise the wound with water and air and hemp, and help it in all ways that you can until it is healthy; and it is necessary that all hours that you cure him, you tie his legs, and bring medicines to their place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is located in the bladder, and stuck there, and urine cannot come out; if you treat him as I said above, that you cut many times, it is excused from cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I before you work with this mold and make it with three angles inserted into a log:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a file and polish the edge of the stone, so that it cannot come out from behind the stone; then push the bit into the stone lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the bit in your hand little by little, as far as you can bore through the stone from the other side; and soon enough the urine will come, then press your hand on what is delayed behind the stone that is inside the bit.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this in any way that harms it, then I will polish the stone and another on top of it, then remove the bit between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, and wash away the frozen blood that is in the wound; and heal it until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	there is a stone in women, and if it ever happens, there is great danger, and it is defended by three things: the first is that perhaps the woman is virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to treat herself when she is pregnant, even if she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to treat herself in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in women is more perfect than the stone in men, so that it needs to make a deeper cut, and there is much fear of it. And if necessity demands it, you should find a wise midwife, and lightly [if] she does not help him, then do not [do anything], but rather I will go to a castle in a subtle way; and present her an able midwife in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and order her to do what you command her in the interrogation of the stone; and watch very well whether this woman is virgin: then it [is] necessary for her to push her thumb or foundation and want for it, and she recommends that she pushes her thumb into the malady, and she wants and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she bleeds, then it is necessary that she moves slowly from the entrance of the bladder to the anus, until she reaches the root of the thigh; then chop on the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle where the instrument is placed, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her two legs above the stone or anus, and make a small cut first; then press on the loins, if you feel the stone very sharp to the wound as far as the stone can come out, and know that there are many ways of stones: that is to say, small and large, and sharp and rough, long and round, and which have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the similarities so that you can tell the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it does not go well for you, put the vitriolic brooch on it, and keep it an hour until the Sans is bleached; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have the tools that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone to men to help you in your work; and if it does not go well for you, it is of the artery that has been chopped, put the powder on the root and strain the water and bandages, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone and do not extract it, that by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire has subsided, and the blood stops flowing, return to your work, as long as the stone is hard.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia (hernias)
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Is not the water of life but a mixture of white fluid and fat that is present in the navel, which is called “syfac,” and is never truly found within the navel itself, if one believes that it is another substance; and this is the fat of the navel mixed with the white fluid that we have mentioned; and that does not form a solid mass.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the origin of this hernia is so weak that it arises from the navel, and this matter is spread out widely.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And this mixture does not change color: or it is yellow-white, or red-white, or black, or water-white, and so on; and these are the signs by which we know this mixture: for if it is white  as mentioned above, then it is a swollen appendage, like an organ, and does not close up the navel, because it is moist all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the cloth itself, let the abscess be cut with part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syphillous, then feel it well; so that when you know the color of the moisture, try all the inside quarter by quarter, whereby its form is above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, who comes after the quarter, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with fire, let the patient be made well according to his power and the repletion of his body; then put him on his back on something high, and wrap him in blankets; then sit on his left side, and command the minister that he sit on his right, and spread the cloth over both his legs; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the testicles among them until you reach the long bone underneath, and be your cut all straight by dividing the skin of the testicles little by little according to his power; then pierce the white skin with water at a wide hole, and draw out all the water, and then put your fingers, and stop up the hole upstream; and if the egg should jump out at your work, return it to its place when you have finished cutting the skin of the testicles; and if the egg had jumped into your work, then take it back again; and if the egg should be in his place, but the skin be cut, so that the egg should drop out, then put it back in its place, and cover the hole with a patch; and if the skin has been cut and the egg has not dropped out, then cover the hole with a patch, and bandage him like the other wounds until he is well.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find that the egg is corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you lay the eggs that are suspended, in doubt of the corruption of blood; then take out the yolk from all the suspension, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the egg is assembled into two parts together, knowing that these are two ramies; then take out the other part as you did with the first one equally, then wash the blood, and put on the wound another damp cloth in oil rosin; and put away another damp cloth in wine and oil, and put the two yolks, and put double drapelz on top, and tie it all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two drapelz, and make them of damp cloth according to this form and let them be assembled by stitching into the girdle of the braies, and one of the heads preigne on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the claw; and the other two chief on the two angles, and is all assembled the restraint in the loop of the braier; and no medicine this ramie of cautery in place of a iron size, and it is that you preigne the subtle cautery of fire, and take the skin of the yolks, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syrup that contains the blood is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white syrup once, and scorch with this subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can, until you remove all of it; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this operation is safer; and take care to prevent blood loss and cauterize wounds; and if anything makes you uncomfortable, or an abscess or blood loss or something else, treat what makes you uncomfortable according to what has been said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and does not wait for this operation because of its horror, then make a perforation as I told you, and it is that when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the rancid water is there, then place the patient on a raised seat; for then the abscess will open in the part below the sputum, and insert the perforation long from the heart; and make the opening large so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the site, and bind it, and leave it to run out the remaining water, then treat as long as the wound heals; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the wound's mouth, then you must put a feather or the instrument used to remove the water from the dropsical into it, so that it forms as I have said above; and widen the wound slightly, and know that the water returns and is gathered after six months or so, and when it is gathered as before, and so the patient's days pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I know that in this chapter there are many things to fear, so I think it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the procedures for dealing with an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the testes, and most often from the testicles; and this is due to moisture.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to be understood: by acrid and bitter moisture that spreads into the testes, or by impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the testicle; and it does not cause pain, but it is a grief for the abscess; and perhaps there is an abscess that is painful and dangerous, and of a strange color, and never comes from any artery, or swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, if you know by the hotness of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it only comes that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Cil qui est fais d'enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition à l'expression du toucher des deux, et peut om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l'uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l'uef.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	The dislocation of the shoulder can be caused by moisture, and when it is reset but cannot stay in place, it can repeatedly dislocate with slight movement. First, you must reset the dislocation. Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, causing the limb to be misaligned and causing the patient great pain and injury.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the chip is at the back, you must cop it all, and extract the chip, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are finished, if you employ the wound with wet wool wrapped in oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is well.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the scrotum
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a treatment for the scrotum involving wrapping it in a fabric of similar appearance to a cloth, with the coions softened, and the patient grumbles less when he moves; and the treatment for this disease is well known from what the old man did, and we will tell you the work of him according to that.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you have the patient sit on a soft seat, then dip the suspender of the coions in water at both ends, all the vessel that are near the penis, and dry them thoroughly; then cut off each part with a sharp knife as we said when extracting the arteries that are in temples; then put a needle into it with double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and quickly tie it to the other end; then join them in a straight line according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as you would with others where one vessel bleeds, so that no vessel loses its blood because of the incision; and let them dry and not be able to help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	about the wound of the eye
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	about the wound in the eye, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angers, because the intestines descend from that wound to one of the loins; and this wound is either from the section of the syph, or of the extension thereof, and these two ways come from causes: from percussion, or leap, or braying, or lifting up pain, and similar things; and the signs when it is of the extension of the syph, if it is that it comes little by little, in a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the apostemes are equal until almost the end, so that the syph hurries the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	and the signs are when it is of the section of the syph, that it brings about sudden pain, and the apostemes are different appearances, detaching the skin there, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the course to the end of the syph.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never let the intestines descend with the circumcision, and is held back, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	For in these treatments of iron to frighten, for it is necessary to wash away.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the circumcision is that you command the patient that he keep the intestines in his hand at the bottom of the wound, if he can enter; then is it necessary to wash away very well with water. Then take two fingers of your right hand and place them on the skin around the wound, and peel back the skin as far as possible; then bottle the blood from the abdomen into a cup, and take care not to let any blood fall; then pour the blood onto the skin that has been peeled, making sure that it covers all sides; then bottle your index finger in the place where the skin was pulled away, between the white skin that has been peeled and the skin of the scrotum, and between the second white skin, and behind the skin of the scrotum, and between the second white skin; and with your right hand, press down on the skin below the cup, and take the white skin that is above your left hand, and squeeze the blood from all sides onto the skin; and command the minister to extend the blood in front, and tie what remains of the skin. Then cut a piece of thread as thick as three threads made from 30 threads, and bottle it in the back part of the white skin, which is behind the skin of the scrotum; then tie the thread around the skin, leaving two loops at each end; then wrap the ends of the threads around the skin and tie them together, so that no thread remains that might be eaten by the lice that live on it, and allow the wound to drain; and after this, cut a piece of thread as thick as three threads made from 30 threads, and tie it at the top of the skin that has been peeled, leaving a loop about an inch long; then wrap the ends of the threads around the skin and tie them together, so that no thread remains that might be eaten by the lice that live on it, and allow the wound to drain; and after this, cut another piece of thread as thick as three threads made from 30 threads, and tie it at the bottom of the skin that has been peeled, leaving a loop about an inch long; then wrap the ends of the threads around the skin and tie them together, so that no thread remains that might be eaten by the lice that live on it.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And there is no time when the white blood is cauterized that we have said, after the incision, through doubt of decay of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leaves the ligature as long as it bleeds on its own; and if it delays bleeding, then raise it with hot water, and put on what we have said, as long as it bleeds; then cure the wound with other cures until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnose
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone dare to try to make the cure with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old one said that it is made thus: as you join the rope together, in a similar way tie the vessels after cutting lightly on the leg; then tie it up and cure the abscess of whoever performs it, as long as the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until he is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No time comes without injury to the arteries, as we have said, and open them up; and do not let any of the intestines hang out with the coils, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; but nevertheless, if he stays too long in this place, so that the wound or gangrene believes him, until the intestines hang out; and such happens by the extension of gangrene which is to the arteries, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and inflated up the openings, and opening them up; and the cure is with fire, as we have before said; and never is cured with iron in this way: but let the patient lie easily on his back between your hands, then take the place of the injury by the large according to the quantity of III days; and then remove the gangrene which is from the skin that follows, then take a string and put it over the place appearing from the gangrene; and press it perfectly on the belly, then cut the two appearances from the gangrene on top of the string, and cut them both; then remove the top of the string, and do not cover with gangrene or extend any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you fix the threads, if the wound is well-cured until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The cure is necessary, and does not have an appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is moistened at that place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the leather of the cods
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Several times the leather of the cods is softened in some men, because the hairs that are within are softened, and it can be seen; and it is necessary, when you want to cure it, that you make a draw on the back of the animal, and cover the leather which is softened on the natural leather; then join the two lips with one seam, and cut off the superfluity of the leather that has been softened in three or four seams firmly; then sew between the seams, and cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed, and weave it.
dou chastrement	Dou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cauterization is done according to two ways: either by attraction, or by a cut.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, let us sit the beast in hot water, until the joint is softened and relaxed; then grab it with your hand, so that you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: il convient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions à ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef à I cop, lorsqu'tu les auras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc du siac et lou subtil siac qui est sur les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que celle qui est faite par attraction, pour ceu que à l'attraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu'elle soit sanee.
des hermofrodites	Of the chastisement of the waist: it is fitting that you tan the bestial, and press the leather of the testicles to your left hand, then tie the suspension, and bind each oaf to I cop, when you have well scarred them; and leave no hole of the sac and subtle sac which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is milder than that which is made by attraction, for since attraction may fail by chance and no part of the testicles remain attached, by which the bestial desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is according to two ways as men: the one that is between the two crotches open as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes the urine is cut.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the loins hair also as a penis and two crotches.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of the man and the woman is that you copulate the virgos opened all, and cure them so as others wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine jumps by the skin of the crotches, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tentbug
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	is a virgo opened on the natural part, so much that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it also great as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tent bug to your hand or oncines, and cope lightly; and do not go too much em full, that it runs away with blood, then the cure of another cure as long as he is sane; and to a different virgo that comes out at the mouth of the marris, and employs, and by chance jumps out, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called it the «old disease kowee».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary for you to split it, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic behavior
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is erratic when nature in a woman is not yet discerned, or when the hunchback is small; and is determined by birth, or happens through illness that has come about; or is through charioteering, or through subtle or poisonous substances, and is perfected in marriage, or in costings, or seedings, or whatsoever; and the ability to conceive, and childbirth, and perhaps the growth of flowers, too; and the knowledge of this one is through the aspect of bail.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	For if it is close to the appearance of stork, whether it appears on your two hands or on the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is through subtle or poisonous substances, and it is close to the appearance of a stork, whether it appears on your two hands or on the right side. If it is through subtle substances, and it is close to the appearance of a stork, whether it appears on the pages of a book, or if you hurry, and then turn it inside out: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two pages, until the subtle substances are dry, and the stork-like appearance is complete; then take wool, and moisten it with oil, and put it in place, and let the woman lie on her back every day, so that he cannot hold her down.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if it is hard and thick, then you must combine it with the liquid that looks like moss.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stinky and dirty, then hang it by the hair and dip it; and apply medicines that stop blood, as in the case of dragon's blood, incense, together with honey, then put a large cotton rope around the wound so that the wound cannot close; and let it be for a long time, and put on a linen bandage; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the wound begins to smell bad, if you cover it in this way, then except for abscesses, they will not get infected.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For abscesses that are in the genitals, one must not apply fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	are openings of veins, and when they are old, they become thorny; and we have spoken in the division of signs of lice, and I will now say here those that bring healing.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the hernia, when they are completely in the womb, and do not feel except for the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the womb, one can feel them, are those who can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then bind the belly with thorns, and wrap it in roots of herbs that restrain blood, as well as dragon's blood and incense and similar things; then pour water on its feet for an hour, and then put it in cold water; and if the blood comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and confound it with honey and so on, and make an ointment with it and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if it doesn't, with the help of suction cups on the back and without hurting them; then take another one, and with juice from plantain or from wild grapevines mixed with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, to cover the place with ointment until it is healthy; and what is called 'aloe' is red, and resembles a sharp plant, then cover it as I have said in the recipe; and then heal it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	The abscesses of the breasts
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	come in the breast, as if it is a cancer and an abscess of the bone and the herpes and the gangrenes and the boils and the fistulas and the hemorrhoids and the chili-like abscess, and many other diseases that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I die in this treatise the apoplexy who comes in the limb, which is not an apoplexy but a bowel twitch; and if you know how to work with iron, you will see that the apoplexy is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red, you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die while the pain is relieved; and then make it sit on II seats where it leans, and supports its leg; and let its knees be spread out, and tie its braids behind its knees, and bind them firmly with a good rope; then suck its breath towards its right side, and introduce the instrument with which you work on the mouth of the limb, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you put the hook first to see the depth of the limb, so that what enters into the instrument does not come in more deeply than it should, and does not wound the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover its depth with cloth, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he put the tip of the instrument on top, and wet it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and the hand is made soft, if it is necessary to cover the head, lead to the spittle; and when the bowels are empty, if it is necessary that you put in the wound wet tents in oil of roses or in green dry oil; and place the tent outside the wound at the full of the marrow, and place on the side of the marrow and on the other hand net wet with water or pomegranates are cooked; then the cure after two days of poulticing coming to this, as long as it is healthy; and no time raise the marrow and the wound by cupping of water and honey, and then of water or roots of licorice and arnica are cooked; then recover to the poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has healed in the marrow, you must refrain from cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The art of midwifery is first to know the natural shape of childbirth, and the signs thereof, if thou seest the woman press down within her, and yearn to smell the air: then hasteneth the child forth with a light pressure upon her belly; for when it cometh forth by her head, and with it the second child, then knowest thou that the birth is according to nature, and that the issue goeth out from her navel, and the second child with him, and that the married man rideth himself of his excesses by a good purification; but if this cometh not forth in such wise, then comeeth it not naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it cometh not oft times upon its feet, and cometh from the breast or shoulder, or hands, or sometimes upon her belly, or often, and is turned by aventure upon her neck, and in other ill-shaped ways; therefore it behoveth the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how she must aid it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a man falls on his head because of a natural fall, and the woman gives birth to a baby with pain, and the virtue of the man is weak, so that when he sits on a saddle or women hold him; and rise his essence of oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then pour the milk between his two small spatumiles whose shape is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If a man falls on his head because of a natural fall, and the woman gives birth to a baby with pain, and the virtue of the man is weak, so that when he sits on a saddle or women hold him; and rise his essence of oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then pour the milk between his two small spatumiles whose shape is here: and split the second, and pinch his nail until the moisture that is in it runs out; and hold the belly of the woman until the baby comes out, and if it does not come out, it is appropriate to clisterize the woman with fenugreek musk with oil of Sisament; then make her drink and shake off the water, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: so now the baby.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	Et si les deux mains sont fortes, il convient que tu les ramènes doucement peu à peu; et si elles ne peuvent entrer, met la femme sur un siège, et lui relève les pieds; puis démarre le siège du sol, et étends la femme, pour qu'elle ne trébuche pas en se levant; et si les mains ne peuvent entrer, et l'enfant est mort, si on leur applique un couteau qui est ici placé, et extrait l'enfant, et le ramène également.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	and if the issue of the child is on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, then it is convenient to turn it over; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then press down on its feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can't he jump just as high as his knees, if you order him to bend, and make him shake with fear; if he jumps too high, may God help him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not so as we have said, then let it be done little by little, so that it may be according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For now it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	For now it is light. de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the baby comes in this form, put the basket on his knees little by little; then support him on his neck, and hang his legs down, and let him lie on the bed; and fold his hands little by little, and then take them to his belly, and hold the cords behind, until he is completely delivered; and the baby does not jump, if it grabs its feet and changes its shape, then it changes its belly above, then it puts your hands; and bring the baby little by little; and tell the woman to lean back as the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child who comes wide a hand hanging

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this way to all the second part, if the fire has become empty; and if the child is put on its face and neck, so that it does not stay there, and dies the child; then put the child inside, until you have done it as it should be done, and order the woman to lean back once: and then do it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	That twins are born many times, and never three or four at a time; nor is it an odd thing, nor has it ever happened before.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are an odd thing, and do not live long, if they are alone; but I know that if they are multiplied, they are devised by the doctor who is near the bad one; and they are never born naturally as all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	If they are born with difficulty, as we have said before, and the doctor is subtle, and does what he can quickly and lightly; and do so that it may be for his salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No child is ever formed in the womb of one or two or three or four or five or six or seven or more up to fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the wise Lord, and the doctor knows everything; for sometimes it may be an odd thing; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; then put the swaddling clothes in his hair or in his neck or in his mouth or in his throat or near his ribs, and the descent is on the feet, if he takes or holds it at the cost of his hands; and it is necessary that he tie the swaddling clothes to his right hand, and place the bundle between his two left hands, and pour them all over with his right hand slightly, and put the swaddling clothes in any of the places that we have said, until it comes out to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the swaddling clothes:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then place it between two others, or the tier is in need of it, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them equally with a movement from one side to the other, so they move out, and make the teeth of the onces by so holding them, as this is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers. And if the child's head is large and it is in the birth canal, or it has a sharp head assembled, then it is necessary that you squeeze the thorny spit between your two hands, and cut off the sharp one; or pull it out with the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or paste that follows this; and in the same way make the child's head large naturally; and then pull the bones out with tongs, and the child's head jumps out and is pulled by force, so let it be cut, as much as the moisture that is at the exit runs; and if it cannot come out, then split it into pieces with your fingers; and if it is swollen in the belly or along the sides, then it is necessary that you pierce it as much as the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he falls on his feet, then is the light attracting, and the adjustment to the mouth of the mare is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If he falls on his belly or chest, then cover him with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and turn the belly or chest until the moisture that is there comes out; and if another member is dislocated and does not move, then pinch the mare's mouth with your hand firmly and pull it out; then either tie it or cut it, and treat it; and if the mare's mouth is shrunk by an abscess that has come to it, then do not work, but apply moist and greasy things; and apply plasters, and slice in water that is softening and moisturizing.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If he falls on his back and you can make it even, then apply what we have said to the live child; and if one cannot do that, then cut it into pieces and leave nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, bring the person who has this illness that we have spoken of in the chapter about the abscesses that come with the mare; and if the blood comes out, let it be restrained with water, and other treatments are brought to it.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose child had died inside her, then consulted another person on that, and another one refused to treat it.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the abscess opened up, and it swelled greatly, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called in to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I couldn't stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a poultice of strong attraction, and it came out with a bone, and after a few days others.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, for the mare's womb does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to look at the wound, and in doing so I injured myself, for a long time afterwards; it was only then that I remembered this unguent, for whenever a master would examine an unusual thing, he knew how to use it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the shoulder to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	This is followed by the description of the form of the pressor, and how to bend the arms; and at two turns are the shoulders of the two limbs.
