Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the corners should be thinner than the restrainers, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the pipe should be wide enough, and the margin of the branches should be long by a palm and a half; and these two connectors should be joined together at their ends, making them about a palm and a half long; and these two joints are to be inserted into the mouth of the armature in order to open when the corners are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Une autre forme, à sa ressemblance plus subtile et plus légère, soit faite de fuste d'ébène ou de buis, selon l'apparence des tenaille; et ait à II chaise II ajouts, si comme tu vois, d'une paume de long, et II doigt de large; et lorsqu'tu vois ouvrir la marre à tout l'instrument, si fait s'asseoir la femme sur le lit, les pieds pendant et les jambes ouvertes, puis boutte les II ajouts ajoutes ensemble en la marre, et tien le chef de l'instrument désos entre ses cuisses; puis ouvre ta main à tout l'instrument, si comme tu as fait aux tenaille uniformément, selon la quantité que tu vois ouvrir la bouche de la marre, jusqu'à ce que le balancement fasse ce qu'elle veuille.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This is another form, of more delicate and lighter appearance, made from ebony or boxwood timber, according to the appearance of the pliers; and it has II ajouts at each end, as you see, a palm long and II fingers wide; and when you see open the socket to the entire instrument, so that the woman sits on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then button up the II ajouts together in the socket, and hold the handle of the instrument between her thighs; then open your hand to the entire instrument, as you have done with the pliers uniformly, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the socket, until the swing makes what she wants.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If I do not have the instrument, do not put it on me, for their need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second one is held back from childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the woman to retain her semen, and then make it spurt out with contraction, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she vomits because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not happen, I can take it, and make a vessel or cup out of it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the woman, as aniseed, rue, fennel, chamomile, cassialign and centaurium; all these herbs, or any of them, are cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then one end is placed in the vessel, and the other in her mouth, and she is made to spit out the vapors that come into her; then she is made to spit up, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If it jumps the second time.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If it remains after this cure and is not well, order the bailiff to moisten his left hand with oil of mint or with musk from Alto, and then let it rest in nature, and then try again; and when you have found it, if you pinch it and stretch it little by little correctly, so that the marrows do not break at the extraction; but you must move it slightly to the right and to the left, and then draw it out. And then it will come off.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the marrows is stiff and hard to extract, we have already spoken about the cure of sweating and the use of herbs; and if it is only this that you have said, be careful not to mess up when you draw it out; but it is necessary that he who is at the mouth of the marrows should bind himself to the lap of the woman, then the ointment of tetrafarmacon should be applied to him; so she will eat and recover, and will get well. But, however, if this one comes about, a bad odor will rise from the stomach and head, and it will make the patient blither.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If then are necessary fumigations suitable for this: no one of the ancients has experienced fumeation with nettle and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument that you shall use to smoke the woman at the retention of flowers and the second one is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like a dog's head, and one sets the thin end in the smoke, and the large ends above the fire; and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the smoke until it is spent, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mourning children are born who have not yet had the foundation pierced, but a subtle surgeon heals them: if then it is necessary for the ball to pierce that subtle one at his right hand, and does not pierce it with a spud, and sews up the wound so that it does not touch; then put on another wet cloth in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not recover, so put or prop a cane of pulp, and leave his hands free, and let him rest when he feels pain going up to the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And no time comes this sudden healing of a wound or an abscess; if it is covered quickly: if it is cured, as we have said, with the cane of pulp.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are difficult to treat, and they cause more pain than those that come from the fundament or between the two parts, if there is one or more; and when this nodation is old, if it opens, and again moistens with a clear or subtle liquid, and never does these fistulas persist; and they are caused by him who has an ejection or venting when the patient makes an ejection, and by chance in the spring.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it perforates only up to the bladder, and up to the half of the penis; and it reaches up to the joint of the scrotum, and up to the knot of the cow's tongue.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And then recognize the location of the fistula, and not recognize it at all; and this is that you stick your little finger or foundation with a thin needle made of gold or iron in the fistula when there is no deviation.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is deviation, and you stick a thread of linen or hair of horse as far as your finger feels the thread or hair at your side; and if you don't feel it, and there does not come an outlet of wind or urine or blood, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; but hurry to heal.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula perforates only up to the bladder or up to the conduit of the urine, so that the urine falls, and cannot be treated with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just at the joint of the loins, then let him try to come to his place; if there is no twisting and no pain in the side, then he should not take medicine or apply ointment immediately; and with these persisting fistulas there is no cure except work, and the vain devices of foolish people who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	If it is not persisting and is not old, there is hope of health by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his loins, and tilts his loins to his belly; then pour a bucket of rain, or a ladle of water if there is twisting, until you know where the piercing comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain around his fundament, then you should put your two index fingers there, and feel immediately that the piercing has been pierced; and know whether it is persisting or not; if it does not work, then do not try to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignation enjanrant char et soudant.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is done thus, then it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that does not work then it cannot be cured; and if the tent is caught between, and does not cut all the way down to the base which is at the bottom of the tent, and there is a covering of char or tar between your two knees, and you see the fistula through the covering on ceu who suffers the pain; then cut off the cover from the entrapment of the fistula, and pour in the fire before the tent, and will be delivered the tent, and it will be destroyed; then burn those faulty skins which seem like a feather of an owl, and there remains none.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound does not heal, and there is a gap between yourself and the work, then the fire cautery or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these joints joined together, and the drying up of blood and the removal of moisture; then heal the wet tent like a baked pie or a crushed fruit, until the bones come out, and the joints are burnt in the bowie; then heal the wound with dry medicines that do not burn.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is reset, if it is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from the very foundation of the chest and is distant from the heart, then it should be cut off or removed from its foundation, and this should be examined.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there are two threads or a thread or a string, or it is ready to pierce, then know that there is only a way of hope and effort in three ways: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut off up to the foundation, or you stop it with tents as we have first said; and do not go too deep, so you cover the foundation which covers the tent, or by tent or any other instrument pointed; then expose this rotten wood which is in the wound, as far as you can; then examine to restore the wound, and to delay the fistula in the part farther from the foundation: for this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there is no fistula in this way: and when you plug the tent into the fistula, and it is at the base of the skin on top, so take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put the thread in two, and plug the tent into all the thread in the fistula until it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the fundament inside, then pull out the thread of that piercing, so that you plug your two at the fundament; and tie the head of the thread together, and extract one from the other, and leave them for a day or two; and do not restrain either one, until the thread has covered those two teeth that are between them, and they have bitten; then cure the wound as soon as it is healed and well.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, but you make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too perfectly closed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to do thus for the lancing if done quite perfectly, and then the cure, as we have said, until he is well.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the needle with thorns from which one makes a fistula is hot and sharp on one side, and not on the other; and for this reason it does not behoove to do thus if done quite perfectly, and then the cure, as we have said, until he is well.
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are of two manners: either they are within the fundament, as grain of resin, and have some small and some big, and go forward towards the root, and one or more, are outside the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those that are outside, if they have a little moisture, and then dry up again, or have a little blood, and have the color of the flesh, the cure for those who have them within the fundament is this: you command the patient to let them flow by straining, until the root comes out, and the thread comes; then hasten and hold it with pliers, or you hold it with your nail, then cut off at the roots; and if they do not stay because of their moisture, take them with a ribbon, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; and draw them towards your feet, then cut off, and powder over them some hot powders that are in the fire for cauterizing; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cauterization, since they are cured by other cures until they are well; and if the root cannot come out, take the patient's cure with a blistering, biting and sharp thing to wash what is within the root, so that it can come out freely; when the patient is blistered, and the thread has gone away from the root, the cure is light.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary for you to administer the wound according to this method: take a piece of twisted thread and bottle it in a needle, then bring the thread up from below and make the needle pierce from the other side, then bring the two ends of the thread through the needle, and if it is large; then twist the thread into a knot, then remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one there to drain the blood; then put a damp bandage wrapped in oil or lard on the foundation, and place it on the foundation, and order the patient to rest; and then leave it alone until it starts to bleed, and when it stops bleeding, treat with ointment and other treatment until it is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	At the bottom or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying out at the bottom or in the intestine, and by necessity of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you resect a wart or your nail the skin from above, which does not let it get wet; then cure it as soon as it becomes hard again as it should; and if it cannot be hardened, then start shaving again harder than before, until it heals and is scraped; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	Do you fart?
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	This text seems to describe a medical treatment for a condition that causes a person to fart excessively, which is referred to as "formice." It suggests that this condition may be caused by a small opening or tear somewhere on the body, from which wind can escape freely and uncontrollably. The text also mentions that those affected can feel a sharp pain with each fart and that it affects the entire body, including the hands more than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a twig of a duck's feather, or a feather of a strong vulture, and put that twig on the fart, until the purple ring circles the fart completely; then bring your hand back to all of the twig until you have covered completely around the fart, and fix it in place, and scrape the fart from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this of a dog's or iron's size according to this form, and be subtle and run over it:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	ne mie pierce, por mayz tener ao due, et mayz presier: And if you see, so cauterize the noise, so as it is before or the chapter of cautery of fire.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the bladder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time made one bladder of silver or leather, or melted lead or hair; and no time made these instruments little and big, according to the which they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then that one brings in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are little.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bladder small and big is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say that there is a distention where the belly is tied, as you see it, and the chaps are pierced from within; and there is a perforation on one side and another on the other; and let the medicine be placed in a bladder of wine or parchment, and pierce all around the small perforations, and put between each perforation a thread of strong twine wrapped around X or around it; and bind the belly as if it were a sheep; and when the medicine is inside, if it clings to the instrument before a strong thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil or ambergris or some other thing be applied to the blade of the cauterizer; then pour it lightly; then the minister spreads the medicine with both hands until it is completely covered; then he removes the cauterizer, and raises the patient's legs against the wall, and pours out the medicine, as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you make him a poultice when he has pain in his abdomen, and the medicine comes out soon, then remind him until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or an abscess, then make a poultice as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin poultice so that the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said about the division the cure of wounds; or I will tell you the cures of hands and medicines, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the places where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by hitting with a stone, and cutting with an épée and a coustel or a lance or a fust or a siette or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that stings on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds, for the reminder will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs or the chief bone is not broken, take care lest it be from a rock or similar thing, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is great, and you doubt whether an abscess is hot: if it happens so that a healthy person is sick from the wound, and it is opposite to the affected part; and dismiss the patient's repletion of wine and fatty meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	I say that if he does not improve, if his flesh is wasting away and he does not drink wine, nor eat fat meat; and put over the wound, if an abscess forms thereon, moisten it with oil or vinical spirit; and if there be no abscess, if the wound is fresh and not moved by air, dust, I will say a little later; and if he has moved it, put over some onions, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as of a sword-slash and similar, and the lips cannot be made to come together by stretched out, if they are made to come together by sewing, as I would say to the wounds of the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it holds only a little, then bandage it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat heavy meats, as well as cooked grain and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find rot in the leather, and it has not reached the bone, then bandage it well and carefully, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, which must be tied off, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie it off, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light; and that you put this powder into them so that fire will not move them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and the powder finely, and apply the wound, and squeeze it to form, until it has healed well and joined together all its blood; and then bind it firmly, and leave it unbinding, if it does not swell; for you do not apply medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make any fire solely with incense when you have dragon' blood but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound at all, even a little, then you should not put any of this powder on it; but put on some softened onions or dough of barley flour made with water and honey until it has healed; and then cure it with other cures until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers; and I will tell you later about breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	the wound comes from the throat and is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the throat where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the neck, if there is no other device than to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, for it harms the neck and makes it retreat; and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the neck is cold, and its extension of the air is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be sweet, if like warm water in cold water, and mixed with oil, and washed too in warm water, and other small stones according to this way, and wet with oily.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with bandages, and then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bowels full of blood, then the perforation or deeper; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, so that it dries up and stops, then cauterize it properly; and if the inflammation in the throat is cut, or the voice, and the treatment is kept, for meat goes well, if the taste is kept on the neck of the throat, and does not touch the throat but sets it according to its natural shape; and then remove it forward, and leave it for some days, then treat it with ointments that are useless until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then seek it; and if there are pieces of bone, then push them hard everywhere it can be, and those you cannot reach, then leave it as long as the wound putrefies, and its issue is obstructed and stiffened; and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound, and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter on the treatment of wounds.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If the wound is from a lance or knife and it is deep, then look to the wound to see if the patient feels pain: since thus that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep and is fresh throughout the entire body, do not apply powder at first, nor bind it so as not to cause pain unless it has completely healed, and allow the patient to rest; but if you do not have ointment, put raw cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on his back for three days, or four, or more; then you will no longer see any spasms or painful twitching from the body; and when you see the right signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the boils and other ailments as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot be healed, then cut out what is bad so that there is no fistula; if the cure is done like this.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	For if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is deep, then sew it up; and if it is shallow, then use powder, and if it has broken into pieces of bone, then cut out the wound, and treat the raw parts as described above; and if they are not raw, then let the wound fester, so that the extractions will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement dou ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	For the rupture of the abdomen is great and little and small; so that there is a great wound which does not let the intestines out, or the ropes of the intestines, so that the intrusion of air; and the suture is more difficult, and never less than a small wound than a great one, for if we leave the intestines in place, coming one after another, it is because they are cold; and for this reason the intestines swell sometimes so that they feel the cold, if we do not put them back into place, and because they are smaller, the little wound feels more than the big one; and know that the rupture of the abdomen has three ways: the common sutures have their source in the abdominal suture, and the common and specific sutures of the other wounds are common to the other wounds; but nevertheless they are more specific to the abdominal wound, and I will say each one separately and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines comes out, and there is something to be done, it should be done with one of these two methods: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, heat it with the following method: dip a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook it in squirt and cumin and spices, and draw out the intestines until they are swollen; and never stop doing this, and rest as much as you can so that it swells up.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with water or warm it, and cook the herbs, because in this way the entrance is closed to a small amount; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure should be to rest, that we do not cut it unless there is a great need; and this is the instrument to split it: If you cut inside the loop and don't go out, and see this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are protruded, if you return them to their natural place in their proper position, if you can do so, for it is necessary to do this.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, then raise the head and chest higher than the lower part; and thus, the wound that ruptures from the abdomen is in one of the two parts; and so it is necessary to arrange that which I said for large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you will arrange yourself in the same way, and then, between your hands, minister to the wound with sharp knives that cut through all of it, and join the lips; and this is the common way to stitch up, and it is necessary for you to squeeze a double thread around the needle from both sides, according to the size of the wound, and leave a space of one finger's breadth at each end; then take another needle and thread, and sew on in the same way as before, leaving a space of one finger's breadth between each stitch; then tie off the thread, and do not cut it short, but let it hang down so that it will not get in the way; then cut off the ends of the threads so that they are even with each other; this method of stitching is better for small wounds, for if you use too fine a thread, it will not hold well; and it is not good to push the needle too deep into the flesh and skin, lest it pierce the wound before it is sewn up; and then tie off the threads at the end, and do not cut them short, but let them hang down so that they will not get in the way; and if you wish to make a large wound heal quickly, then sew it up with very fine thread; and this method of stitching is better for large wounds than for small ones.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him the intestine, then it was outside for 22 hours, and the wound closed after 15 days, and I treated it, and he healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miracle was that he did not die, and I did not treat it with ointment, because I was in a place where they do not have any, and I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two ways of stitching: take the needle, and draw it from the outside to the inside; when it has gone through the flesh, turn it around so that the thread comes out again on the other side; and the stitch is made as the tanner does with the fur, and let the thread come out once on one side, and bring it back again on the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which the Gauls do properly, if it is so that there is no thread, which brings together the two parts naturally, and applies one of the heads to the other head in this way: make an eye or a hole near one of the heads of the mirror, and pierce it down below, and leave the two heads of the stitch; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside part jutting into that inside, as the two heads of the stitch; then pierce both from the outside part jutting into that inside, in two other heads of the mirror that are on either side; and this is the way to sew and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Gauls say this word, and no one testifies to the contrary, that we should sew the belly to two needles, or thread in each; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the way of those who sew with a thimble; and know that when the tear is in the middle of the belly, the stitch is more difficult than the others of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Judging the wound is the same as judging other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it, let the intestine back, and the bowels; then put on the powder with a dry cloth, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and tie the thread, and bind the poultice, and the mirabene; then cure the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to heal, a cotton cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in most cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will spread to the main members, then you should moisten another light one with oil of tempera (a type of warm oil), or with rose oil, and put it around the arms, and soak the axilla (armpit); and if pain or pus appears in the bulge, and often happens, then let the wound drain (black) wine, and most certainly the pus comes out to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal tract called "small intestine" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is because of the development of veins, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to that of a newborn.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tip of the wound jumps out from the wound, put it back as soon as possible while it is still fresh; and if it has become old and dark, you must find the location of the dark spot, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the two edges, and let the two heads hang down from the side of the wound until far away so that the extraction can take place when the tip jumps out, and the wound bleeds.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in some ways, for I have seen that some are torn or have a stomach stab; and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, and excreta and wind came out of it; so I applied treatment according to what I could find, and I did not stop being subtle until it was healed, and I closed up its openings.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him join again, I doubted that the disease had not hurt his belly; and there was no evil, but it stayed in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and none of the experimenters said that when he has a little wound in the intestine, he must be tied up somehow: take some rope from big testicles, then close the lips of the wound, and when the rope has opened the mouth, so put it on II lips, so that he can take out his mouth; and then he holds his head, and this is so that he cannot untie, and puts another rope after in that way that before, until the wound is all closed; and let the wound heal.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief of the intestine is inflamed, and no harm comes to the patient, and he can be tied up with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal in some way: take the chief of this thread of intestine that is almost completely removed, then tie it to the chief of this thread of fine twisted linen thread, then wrap the thread around the needle, and when you cut the intestine, and sew it back together; and this method of sewing with a rope is only good according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, most certainly when it is in one of the small intestine's folds, there is no remedy or medicine except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula, or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Sache that all wound or abscess, when they heal, are called "fistula" universally, and more so when they have been cut and drain.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the virtue of the nutrition root hard and white, where there is no pain, and it is also chewed like a pen of an owl; and never once is it clear drain, and another time thick; never once does it break, and another time it breaks. And I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed, and there is no hope, this is only because of one of the VIII causes: namely, the smallness of the blood or pus; or for its malice; or for what it has hard within, and on the lips, which does not allow birth to take place; or too much drain; or the root is rotted, and the substance is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because, that which is a manner of pestilence, the digestion is late by nature, and late it is healed, and escapes by virtue in the region; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistula, which is made by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if one part is cut off that comes from the principal limb, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the type of fistula that is in this way are difficult treatment, and there is only to work, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the main limb, and similar things. All such fistulas are difficult to heal, and there is no other solution but work, and ignorance; and if there is a fistula that does not come from a limb at all, but from some other part, then cauterize it with fire, so that if it is straight, then you can feel it easily; and if it is bent, then feel it with a thin tent of lead, because the lead bends to the curvature of it; and if the fistula has broken hands and you cannot feel it well with tents, then cleanse it thoroughly with your power, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is completely cut off, and ask the sick person about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you really know the location of the fistula, and if it is far from any joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the locations that I have told you, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the false tissue and corrupted bones that are inside; and then heal it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right side, it is necessary that you cauterize it completely, as much as you can, then put wet tents in medicine water, and pour it over the top of the fistula until the medicine corrode the excess that has been retained at the bottom; and then put fragrant oils in sifting water, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted because of the fistula, then remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If you are injured in the main member, as we have said; and if the bones are exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then king as long as the corruption is all bone, then cure of things that hinder car so long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and rent bow as before, knowing you have not gone far: If you discover it and seek until you are at the bottom, and oste all the corruption, then restore the place; and if he is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too great that you cannot come in; if there is no other device than to let nature take its course; and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with a suitable tool for this, and if there are many bones, if you pull them out, do not leave any behind; and if the moisture makes you contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cut off and wet and mend it, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot take them off in an hour, then place something that is corrupting on the wound and let it stay there for as long as the bones are corroded around it, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then wait until the corruption has completely infected the bone, and then cover the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption and it comes up to the root of the bone; then it is necessary to sew and cover everything up to the point of corruption, and then heal it until it is solid. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg; so take this as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from an unknown cause that penetrated deep into the body, until the matter came out on the leg and caused a large abscess, and he had no known reason to operate; but through his foolishness they operated so much that they corroded a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and it came to such an extent that everyone was afraid, and many times it would discharge moisture from the body; and many times I saw him cured after two years, and there was no skill in the art of surgery, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines they used to cure him, and what was causing the corruption, which turned the young man's leg red, and his skin took on a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those clefts, and then searched all the clefts, and found that one came up against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly went there, and dived into one of the clefts until I found a part of the bone, and I found it rotten and damaged, and the decay extended up to the bone inside; I recognized what appeared to me to be the bone, and made sure that there was no further decay beyond it, except for that which I had already seen; then I began to treat the wound with medicines applied over a long period of time, and could not mend it; and then I started again, and found the bone just as before, and found the decay still continuing in the bone, and recognized it, and then took out the bone, and leaned over it to mend the break; but I couldn't reach all the way around one side of the bone, so I treated it with medicines; and it healed and mended firmly, and there was no need to go back and forth over the wound anymore except because of the weakness of the patient, who couldn't stand it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the trunk, then it should be handled thus: take a thread, and draw it to the head of the bone that is open, and command anyone to stretch it up; and place another thread, thicker than the first, on top of the thread that is stretching upward, and tighten them both together; and they are to hold the stretched-out thread in place until they can no longer see or feel the corruption, and do so again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole horse; then set a brand upon it, and then silk from one part to another of the corruption, and let the silk run into the long length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the jointure, then break the jointure that is corrupted, and silk the bone or she which holds it on the other side; and if the corruption is in the extension of II joints, then there is no other pain but to break; and if the corruption is where the hand or the foot grasps, then this thing is very hard, but nevertheless it is necessary that you inquire about this corruption, how it opens; and purify it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not do you harm; and know that the chisel and the silks to cover these bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and subtility, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this it is necessary that you prepare yourself for each kind of work, and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the sign of the ways of the diseases; and imagine the instrument which you have need of according to what is convenient for it.
dou feu	of fire
