For when the limbs are large, it does not come to put on stars before 5 or 7 days or more depending on the depth of the abscess by sometimes; and here is the way of ancient plasters for restoring breach, dislocation, and torsion: and this you take flour that stands on the walls of the mill, and confound it with much ash, and put this confession, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plasterer restoring the breach to various dispositions, most importantly to women and small children, for it is not too thin or too hard.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to restore fracture, dislocation and torsion: take honey and locust beans and enul and asafetida and arabic gum and mugwort, in X z; myrrh and aloe, in V z; alchemi, in VIII z.; and make a powder, and mix it with sheep's dung; the combination of the human body is warm, so use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is useful for torsion: take mugwort and sheep's fat, in X z; myrrh and aloe, in VIIII z.; acacia, in VI z.; armeniaca (senna) powder, in X z., and finely grind it, and mix it with water or sheep's dung, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that have come out of their place, to soothe the pain gradually, and to make the size of the wound smaller: take new milk and mix it with water and oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Emplasters do not help, but they are good for soothing an abscess, and properly relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an embellishment that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth-pine leaves, grind them together, and make an embrocation.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an embellishment for healing broken bones and soothing the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marshmallows, chamomile flowers, violets, wheat flour, and each a part; grind them together, and confound them with wine, and heat the members, or confound them with water or liquorice moistened with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an embellishment that is more effective than the first one, in case of persistent abscess before healing the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marshmallows, and seed of flax, dock, melilote, and sweet grass, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each an equal part; grind them together, and confound them with salt water, or with sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its need for rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iocrene declares in his book that one should not put a broken limb in any wrappings except those made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that they should neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put dry things that are slightly warm on a broken limb, in order to restore it, such as myrrh and olive oil, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plasters which are good for lesions and pain: take wool from sheep, or feathers of birds, or lard, and string it together evenly, and grind it up, and make a plaster out of it, and put it on the leg.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take it a little apart, and make sure that the patient feels no pain, nor has any movement in his bone; if pain comes to the spot again or an inflammation occurs, hurry and take off the plaster now; take a light cloth, and a sea sponge wet with water, and dip it in the water, and raise it up, until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved; then leave it to rest for an hour, and then put on another dry cloth, soaked in warm oil or butter, and tie it on, a little at a time, until you are sure that the patient is healed; and continue this with a small amount of plaster, and do not take it off as strongly as before; and do this very gently, so that he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscesses, redness, pain, and swelling have come from everywhere, and you need to use plasters and binding, if it begins again, as you did at first even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member at all that we have said, unless it is after three days or four or five or seven; and never more than twenty days, according to what you see, until the break comes, and the support of the shoulder approaches; then restrain it more than before, and let it grow flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the moisture dries up more than necessary, then wash it with hot water every time you release it, and let it be for each third day, and let it dry a little; by this work therefore cut off the moisture to the member, and carefully mend what is wrong, that restore the member in a tortuous way: it is bad, and if it is very painful, and I do not see anything but to let it rest and then make it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various ways to break a bone
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are various ways of breaking a bone and they have different shapes, and the causes are distinct; because there is a break that is made by a spear's impact, and all the bone is shattered up to its shaft, as if it were an arrowhead or a lance; and for this reason this way of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	For the spear pierces the bone from above, and is called this way of breaking "absolue"; and is the wound from such great or small breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a break due to impact, or a crack, or a blow on stone, or falling onto stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches the tendon that is outside the bone, or is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that is made in the bone is as fine as a hair, and is a small fracture, and for this reason it is called 'capillaire'; and if the wound that is made by hitting a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and makes a piece of bone come out; and the head of the bone is so wedged in as a blacksmith does when he forges on the fire; then let it be inserted between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is more moisture at the top of the bone, as at the head of a child; and there are all these types of fractures that small pieces are broken off, like these; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the types of fractures by the traction on them, and the investigation of the tent, and by the corrumped cart that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by what happens when bone is exposed, and you rub it with salt, thus opening the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for the fracture, be cautious of accidents due to disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of reason, expansion, paleness, feverishness, and hair growing fur and turning red, and other similar signs in multiple conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you don't see a promising accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the baby is born first to you, and it's in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it' s in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day at most, so that the tissue around the bone does not rot, and the accident that we mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes only to the membrane that covers the brain, so it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and it is that you press the head of the patient severely, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more smoothly than you can, and because the evacuation of blood comes to uncover the bone, or abscesses come, help him with what is necessary, and is that you fill the place of the membrane with wet linen oil-soaked; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you cut the strictest part in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there are other similarly large ones.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that if you have a number of different shapes, some are short and others are long, and are pointed, and are of iron; and in doing it lightly, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce it from behind, so that you bring the nails with the points, not completely through so that they do not pierce beyond the bone at the tip, and must be above the point with a margin or circle, so that it does not let the point go beyond the bone; and you need to have more than one, so that each comes in its place from the edge of the bone, so that you have nails for all of them; and this is the form of the three ways of nailing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing behind the bone is that you place the nail on the bone, and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone has been pierced; then put the nail in another place a little further on, and do the same throughout, then make the incisions narrow as possible so that you cannot feel them, and lightly, as we have said, until you can take the bone out by hand, or any of the tools you have, such as pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the skull or the sinews.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have cut the bone and treated it, if you recognize that you should preserve the sharpness of the bone from all other tools that resemble an incisors, but it is necessary that it be more tender and thinner than the other incisors; and if it does not retain any small bones or scales, if the bone is lightly attached to the instruments; then cure the wound with clean and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to cauterize is that which Galen says, which is more effective; and it must be done very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you discover a part of the bone, where the fracture has opened; and when you have discovered this part, you shall place at the end of this lens-shaped incisors:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and this part is wet in both sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then pound with a small mallet from above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and be well aware of the hammer that is desos; if it is ajar to the bone, then the bone lightly, for one would not harm the bone, and fear would not come.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce until the skin, and the bone is cut so little by above, and there are small pieces, then let you cover those roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp razor of which you must have various quantities, to adjust in each place the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are using very large razors, then use smaller ones, and continue doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle fractures, you must adjust it according to its alignment; and this is something that is not well answered to the one who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the syringe is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth double, soaked in wine and oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not harm the syringe, then strip it off, and administer medicines thereon if necessary, as roots of lilacs, flour of timothy, powder of frankincense, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer it immediately medicines of the world without bitter taste; and take care that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave the infection, nor do you let bowels assemble together over the linen thread of the skullcap, for if they corrode and break through, they bring great evil to the patient, because when you put something mordant on the syringe, it may burn from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take good care, so that no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackness comes only because of the medicine that has been put on it, which has its virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and III parts of oil and II drapels of glue onto it, and wrap it in the syrup; then cure it in the way that seems right to you until it is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the neck above are never broken, or one by itself, for they are bones; and this bone is cartilage and does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should drill a small hole in the neck, and put it equal to that break inside your little finger, and at the thumb by its side, until the neck regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if it is broken in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, you must realize that you put the neck even with a stick a little big.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if it is broken in two parts, then do the other way, and you hurry to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth, when the abscesses are calm, then bind the neck with linen bandages, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another of the other part, if it is broken; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the apertures of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that there must be no restoration without wetting the bandages and changing them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that the bandages be wet with sheep dung and powder of mullein; then leave the bandage on until the bones are hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never bottle up or nest pens of geese in the tent, and if there is a draft of air, let it stand, and blows the sick among them, or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess comes while you are working, so that you put cotton wet with oil or a piece of patch in it, or a little bit of hydromel.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, so that you put a paste from flour and si-sement, and powdered incense, cooked with honey, then put it on light bandages, and do not bind the penis; and if the break in the penis is small, and it is broken into little pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments for this purpose, then cut the breach, and cure things that get in the way, and suddenly, if you put pastes and ointments suitable for him; and if there is no pain inside the penis, then cure the tent, and put cloth of linen, until he is well.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very deep, and it is not shattered into pieces except that it may be bent inside, then you can handle it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jaw, you should stick your index finger into the mouth of the patient from the left hand; and if the break is on the left side of the jaw, stick your index finger from the right hand inside, gently pushing it back in place, and make it equal with the other hand from outside, and tie it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is in II, you should bring together the two parts, so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the inside, or rupture, then stretch it with a gold, silver, or silk thread; then put a cloth over the broken jaw, and put another cloth on top of that; and put a big, well-made plate over the cloth, or a piece of leather that is even, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it down tightly, and order the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Et si tu vois que la figure se change, si le désactive au tier jour, et puis remet à point ce qui a été changé ; et met empêtre sur, de la poudre du moulin avec abond d'œuf ou farine de siseament, après ce que tu as osé le cerotage; et met sus l'empêtre autre plus légère, et si les empêtres s'aert, et la disposition du malade ne se change pas, laisse-le tant qu'il soit sané ; plusieurs fois est sané en III semainnes.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses appear, so introduce what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, remove not a piece of the bone; if subtile of the osteotomy are the instruments appropriate to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, so widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have taken all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is deep, make it wide, and put on them compresses that are suitable for this, to draw blood, until they are well.
de la forcele	force him
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	And he forces him several times in front, above the shoulder, and this breakage is according to three ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a breakage with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the ovraige is so that if the breakage is without injury, you have two ministers, so that one of them turns the shoulder so that it does not break; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make the breakage equal on both sides, so that its form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair loss.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	Et s'il a besoin de plus d'étendue, si mets des os un speire rond de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc sa nécessité; et estont et lieve la forcele, et estrongent le speire à ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il convient.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot remove the head of the shoulder at the end, because it comes out completely, it is necessary that the patient lie down on his side, and let the shoulder rest on the ear, and push down the minister's shoulder below, until the bone of the shoulder comes up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on your two sides, and if you find it difficult to join them, it is necessary that you cut them; and remove the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, put this tool back in the shoulder, to keep the medicine away.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not a nail, and be also as wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and has II chisels, as you see, and one is wide and the other is narrow, as is the breaking of the wound that you made when you broke the bone; and when you are confident about the warmth, if the wound is warm, and the break is small, or you doubt about the warmth, then wrap the wound with cloth and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if warm flesh comes, dip it in oil, in ash, and in wine, and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if warm flesh comes, dip it in oil, in ash, and in wine, and put on it. For the extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no fracture, do this: put powder from the mill and ashes of egg on the bone, and apply light splints, and wrap a thin strap around it; then take a thick bandage about an inch wide and long, and wrap the splint with it, so that the head of the splint is hanging down; and wrap a thin strip around the break, and hold it in place; and loop a thicker strap over the back, and tie it tightly; and make the patient walk on his heels, and let him move his arm forward, and keep it from moving by holding it with your hand; and let him walk thus for XX days; then start again with the plaster if you think it necessary, and hold it in place, and let it be restored; and it is restored in 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the dislocation of the shoulder, it shall be that the shoulder does not return to its place and only moves by touch; if the appearance of the fracture is in accordance with its form, and you restore it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can do so; then put on the shoulder powder from the mill with a lot of flour, and light strokes, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and thin board, a little wider than the shoulder, and untie the board at the point where it is tied; if employ this cloth to bind the board of flour, so that the board cuts evenly; and then tighten it firmly with a strong bandage so that the board does not move from its place, and look at the bandage every day; and whenever it amolishes, if tighten it again, and put the board even if it has moved out of place, and lay the patient on his back; and the shoulder is set in XX days or xxv, And when this number is completed, if untie it, and be sure, for this is not bone that moves so lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and there is no pain, if it is raised up, and the bone, and do what we have said in breaking the forceps to calm an abscess, hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is never broken in the middle, but this happens; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it inclines to pain, and there is a lack of relief, and again, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and you place a pillow between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of the II ribs with your hands, and carefully put it in an even position in all ways as it should be; then put it on plasters and cover it with thin lead, or other lighter material, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around the back, and tighten it up, and loosen it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it again; and if it is necessary to remove it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and remove it, and peel off the plaster, and treat it with cures; then put back the plaster, and tighten it up until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rupture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I saith that the break in the ribs comes only from within, near the back and at the top, and they do not bend too much unless they are thin; and the sound is well heard by the two ears.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you should restore it so that the break is even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then put on plaster, and fasten with a stick, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break in the ribs is slanted inward, then the patient feels great pain and a sharp pain, as if he were crying out, because the bone does not support its own weight; and it makes him faint, and he vomits much blood, and this is a sign of serious illness, and they have put up with great discomfort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of these who serve should administer meat that swells the belly, to push the break away from the inside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, except for heated abscesses; if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the skin be warm.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we should not place vacuums on the site, for suction formation, and this seems reasonable to me; however, there is doubt that the vacuum will attract excesses to the site due to weakness in the disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should not cover the site with another moist thing in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the shape equal again, then it is cured with the cure of ulcers, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain from the point of the broken rib, there is doubt for the patient; therefore, it is necessary to split the bone at its end, and to take a tool to protect the wound; and then one should cut the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat with poultices until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses break out, put oil on the bandages to keep them dry and place them in their proper position; and while treating the affected area, make sure that the bandage stays in place until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from a fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when there is a fracture of the neck bone and there is no pain; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to someone and you do not know if he will recover or not, if you see his hands soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in several situations, and if he does not feel pain and does not feel it when it is pulled and does not feel it, know that the joint of the bone has been saved, and the patient has been cured, if one puts a cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if there is a similar sign that comes out at the back of the neck, you must know whether it is healthy or not, if it is, pay attention to whether the bones are soft and whether the accident that has happened to them is due to their own will, and on the back the wind and excretion move without wanting to; and when you have thought about it on his belly, if there is excretion without wanting to.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he has thought about it on his back and he tries to lie down, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	I tell you that this is fatal: do not try to work at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from him, then he is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is this: if there is an abscess that is hot, put oil of rose or meif oil on the spine until it is soothed; then put it on a compress, dry it, and tie it up, and order the patient to rest; and he should not sleep on that side where he feels pain until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et si certains os se dessèvelent, couvrez-les avec de la graisse ; et scellez l'os, puis assemblez les deux lèvres de la blessure, s'il s'agit d'une grande blessure, avec une couture, puis appliquez le traitement à l'huile en utilisant du char, jusqu'à ce qu'elle guérir ; et si l'os est brisé, c'est ce qu'on appelle « la fracture de la côte », si vous prenez un pot avec votre main gauche et le placez à égalité avec l'autre main à votre portée, puis appliquez l'emblancherie et l'étaiement au-dessus, s'il y a besoin ; puis maintenez-le en place, et si certains os se sont dessèvelés, couvrez-les et soignez la blessure jusqu'à ce qu'elle guérir.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For a sprain of the hip, if it is severe, cover it with fat; and then seal the bone, and then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is a large wound, with a stitch, and then apply the oil treatment using char, until it heals  ; and if the bone is broken, this is what is called "a fracture of the hip", if you take a pot with your left hand and place it level with the other hand at your reach, then apply the blainer and support above, if needed; then hold it in place, and if some bones have come loose, cover them, and heal the wound until it is well.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hipbone is broken, and if it is, there should be only a little bit of pain in the head; and make it long, and lower down to the side, and bring great pain to the patient at that place, and also swelling, and an enlargement where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting-to-rights: let your hand be upon it as long as you are upon the broken one; and know what is the break and how it looks; and if the break is at the head, then make it even as much as possible, so that it may look like its natural state.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or if it declines inward, then make the patient lie on his back as much as possible, so that the setting-to-rights of that break may be made known to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put the plaster upon it, and then put a plank or a beam upon it, and draw out the break so that it does not move; and take hold of the place where the bones join together, as long as they are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his back or side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses burst, and there is no pain, as long as the abscesses are empty, and place what we have said before; and then return to healing, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is what is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then you should restore it according to one of the two ways: one is that you take a strong rope, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lie down on two chairs and tie them together, and cut the patient on one side; then put him on a strong rope, until he comes to rest in a position, and have a strong rope ready; then tie the broken end of the arm to it, so that the patient does not move; and then tie the ends of the arms together, so that they are equal in length.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should hold the patient on his back, and tie his hands to his neck, then order two ministers that one should tow who is on the breech with his hands, and the others tow the whole body, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then tie the body with tow, and under it, and extend each minister to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breech is close to the shoulder blade, then it is necessary that you put the tow under the assel, and on the other side at the feet, under the breech; and also if the breech is toward the feet, then it is necessary to put the light tow, without labor, as long as the breech is even on its place, and on its feet; then make it even, if it is necessary, and hold it, because it will not move.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	Et si l'apothicheme est chaud, si ne l'estrangent mie jusques à VII jours, et mets sur lainne mouille en aysil et en oile roset, tant que l'apothicheme soit apaisé; puis l'estrangent, et la manière de l'estranger si est que tu mettes l'empôstre sur la briseure, puis assemble le bras sur l'ajutoire, et met ta main sur l'épaule ou sur lou sein; et mets le drapel, et strange sur l'ajutoire, et sur lou bras, si que le bras soit en lu d'estelles, s'aucune chose ne le défondent, ou se li os n'est muez.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stakes, and put a wider and stronger stake than the others on top of the fracture, and leave two spaces between each stake, and let each stake be as large as to pass III times the width of the fracture; then strangle with the stakes, so as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the cast on the fracture, stronger and more away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the sitting of the stars, and the extraction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and doubt the abscess warm, let it bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then watch each of the three days to see if itch does not swell or come to its place, or if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too much strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you have a sore throat, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such an accident does not come, let us free it only after three days or more, and let the patient lie on his back, with his hands on his stomach; then fasten the shoulder with one cloth of equal size, and every hour, at daybreak and nightfall, check whether the figure of the broken member does not move or become softer; if it heals by the virtue of medicine, and give him meat as we have said before, in a way that the meat is on the first layer; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is fitting that the shoulder and leg should be reset within 40 days of the injury, and then they should be unbound and given baths and medicinal ointments to promote healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stiffening is ugly and swollen, it should not be unbound until 30 days or 6 months have passed.
de la brisure du bras	from the breakage of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small and one large, with the small being at the top and the large below; or perhaps both may break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the healing is light and quick; and when the large one is broken, it is a bad healing, and more painful than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the little bone that has been broken, if it is convenient to stretch it a little bit, and put it on an even plane.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If it is the little bone that has been broken, if it is convenient to stretch it a little bit, and put it on an even plane. If it is the big bone, then stretch it harder; and extend it across the chest, and adjust the splint of the arm higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself in this position, and the splint before him at a height that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the assistants' arms to the injured limb, or to the lieni [a type of splint], and other assistants at the other end above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then let him put on an even splint, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking there are pieces, then let each one be put in its place, and if any of them stick together so that they cannot hold them apart, then bend the bone and set it with force, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the caustic to wound, I have spoken to the single chapter; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there come abscesses, then I bind them with a plaster made of oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and I bind it lightly from above, so that the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then take the wax off, and I lay on the plaster of the powder from the mill with a lot of egg, then put the splints, and let the splint of the break be higher by more than one, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints or arms in several positions: whether the break is in one bone or in two; and draw up more strongly on the break than on any other part, and always less when moving away, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the plaster; and may the strips that are on the break be soft and wet, and not too hard nor too rough, and may the thread from which it is drawn be made of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And support the limb and the ligature for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the limb, as when itching comes to the limb, it is right that you dunk the limb in hot water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb rest without constricting it.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then start the extraction again, and if the ligature is softened and the bone exposed, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it is too constricted so that the member cannot come into being, then make it soft a little, and leave it for some days, until the constriction comes out, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not dislocate it until XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Keep him lying on his back with his hands by his sides and make sure his neck is straight and still, and let him sleep. Know that this break-healer will be restored in 30 days or in 35, perhaps in 20, depending on the combinations and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and at our two sides there are few breaks, and there comes but a little pain sometimes.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or painful, it is fitting that the patient should cross his hands, and he should stand upright and evenly in front of him; then let him put his hand on an extended cloth, and extend the broken bones, and make them even, as well as they can be; and put the plaster and the staples, if there is any blistering, then a piece of cloth is wrapped around it according to the quantity of space; and it is wrapped in a linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the parmenter under the plant's belly, then make a rope of drapels, and command the patient that he strangles it to its broken plant; and then extract it with a long rope, and make its Steele as great as the plant of his hand, and extract it, as it comes.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the back, then it is necessary that you put a Steele on top of it, and another one under the plant', so that his hands are open and straight, then you tie it all around the hand, and stop up the vein between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks at one of the two sides, then let him make it even, as it comes; and pull it with the plant, and if you see that you can put a small straight Steele to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is at the other two sides, then let him make it even, and tie it to the healthy side which is after; or you tie them all together holding, so that he moves, or you put a Steele on top of it, as if he pokes; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme warm, and help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the chest
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the chest are often bruised, and one can clearly see when they move forward and backward; and the healing process is good if one ties a bandage over the bruises, and another around them.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies down on his face, then extends each minister to his part equally; and it is when the fracture has entered the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the chest, then one of the bands goes over the hand, and the others go around the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then one of the bands goes over the knee, and the others go around the fracture; and so, if he extends it downward, then put the bone in its natural position with his two hands, until it is in its original shape, and then put the plaster on it, and tie it up, because there comes blood from an incision.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be calm then return to your work and your treatment; the time is done in a certain way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, let it be calm then return to your work and your treatment; the time is done in a certain way.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it slips and falls on the ground, and turns over what has happened, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that hold, then do whatever is possible; and if not, then split the place where it is, and pull out with force; and cure him as we have said, until he is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the chest here because we put it there, as in the shoulder or arm; however, when restoring it this way does not cause the patient any harm.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the chest is restored in one day, or little more or less, according to the various complexities of the complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the lane from the knuckle
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the lane from the knuckle there is little rupture, but it often bleeds.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is just a split or gash, and goes to all the wounds, and feels no pain, then it feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing is such that one puts an equal piece on both sides until it is assembled so that one can move it; then apply the ointment and put a round bandage on it if you need one, and stretch it as necessary, and also for all other breaks, as an abscess hot and others similar; put on each accident what corresponds to it until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	We know that in the leg there are two bones, one which is called by right "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all similar breaks come as those of the arm, and for this reason the healing is done equally; and if the two bones break together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his nose is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain and sees it well; and turn aside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then arrange the extension, and make it even, and tie the stars evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary that his fracture be ugly, and he has many pieces, so that the extension be less and lighter; and align according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take two faxes of wood that purple the leg on one side and on the other, and are long from the knee to the ankle; then wrap them in two blankets above and below, and tie this bundle in the middle, and it shall not descend the leg to the right or to the left, and so is good; and no one should administer two faxes of wood, and if it is made of wood, and one puts the leg to hold it from moving, and properly he does so on the fracture or wound; and moves each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; then heal as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the feet
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but from the bones of the feet comes a fracture in some cases and not in others; it only occurs when broken in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the feet, and you see these bones overlapping each other, so that the patient lays his foot on the ground like he wants to walk, then now put your foot on its side, where the bones are raised, then press them together as they go back into their places; then apply the plaster and press it down, and place a small tablet flat at the roots of the feet two fingers wide, then tie it tightly around the foot from above, and then remove the wrappings and any other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the joint has healed, for you will find that the bones are even, whether they are broken or not dislocated.
