Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s’il i a aucuns des deux brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit aux deux de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember that you must not forget the other things that I have said about the other breakers, as we have said; and help each accident in turn as it arises.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of breaking the bone of the wrist with a hammer
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of nature is broken in two by a hammer, if the woman is placed in a sitting position with her back supported and her legs outstretched, then fill the breach of nature with cotton that has been made large, and put as much as there is; then let the woman stand up and pull on the back little by little, and then remove the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature and joins the bone again with pulling; and when she wants to urinate, if she removes the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and so do for seven days: so the break will be healed, and death will cease. Take a bladder of goat's milk and tie a cord around it, then pour all of the milk into nature; then blow into the cord forming shapes until the milk is gone inside: nature will then return the break, then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the jawbone of the man or woman is broken, let it be put back as we have said with regard to the hip bone; and these injuries are not hidden from him who puts it to his study and use, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means many things about the right way of restoration: hear then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the vagina, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and pour the vaginal fluid into it; then wrap it in linen, and let it be for three days or so, and he will be cured without surgery.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is right for one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is great, such as the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, to be healed now, so that the healed ones that we have spoken of bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still vitamin water, then you should start repairing the break in the same hour, or that day, if the abscesses are not coming out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses come out, but do not continue to heal until the next day, as long as the abscesses are calm, and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, because you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is protruding from the chest, it is necessary that you put it back into place lightly with your hands, with small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands in terms of length, then take this tool made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and whose width corresponds to the amount of the wound; and for each break, it should be sharp at one end and slightly thick at the other: so that it does not compress the member with your work, and is sharp in front and thick towards the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for the shoulder of the curve should be placed on top of the head of the bone; and he should be pulled once, until he recovers, and be even one with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone well, you must chop off the head of the bone so that the instrument can have the power to do it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone as we have said, with a suitable instrument, be it an incisor or a file, to your power; then strike off that which is delayed in the bone with roughness and small scours.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is restored, and the patient feels great pain after it, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its natural position, then moisten the dressing with black vinager and let it stick properly to it; and do not put anything on the wound except oil where it is necessary, lest it come into corruption and decay; then administer medicines when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, wrapping the covering all around it, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the fracture; and often do this, for they have done such things to the sick man, or dead or decaying, and so the instrument is softer and more pliable than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it does not suit you to put on splints; but wrap it up tightly with hard cloths, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after a day or two wound to the bone, take off what you have put on entirely, and bind with a healing poultice, as with a four-part poultice and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at dusk, until it is healed and restored.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be separated in such a way that the bone does not hurt.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day it hurts, and he cannot bind it but it comes together again, knowing that there are little pieces of bone which cause pain, you must pull the wound open, and remove all these troublesome pieces which bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is a fistula or some other kind of corruption that needs to be treated, according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is broken and opened up on the limb, as in the hip or shoulder bone, and other large limbs, do not draw it out, for many times death comes, but leave it to putrefy; maybe after XX or XXX days, then heal the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	And the bruises that come from the sour wine
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Come often after the santity of the break, especially when it is near a joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the limb's figure; and perhaps cannot make the limbs move naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, therefore, if we are fresh: if you administer stinky medicines, as aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolle, acaice, and similar things; so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine of the stink, or with abun of honey, or with oil; and put them on the knot in piles, and bind them well, and do not remove them for several days; and then loosen them, and start a new one, until the knot is hard; or you hold it on a piece of leather well made; because the property of the leather is that it will make all swelling on the limbs go away; and if the knot is already hardened, it is necessary to cut it off, so that the excess appears, or you cut it with a razor, until it is hard, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the stay
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	And the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains after weak and thin members for various reasons: because one is too tied up tightly, and was not tied up as it should have been; or because he had too many ties, and could not bring the healing to the member; or due to many irritations; or due to too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood increases within him; and administer baths, and give him pleasure and rest; then put poultices on the member so that the poultices attract a lot of healing, and irrigate it often with warm water, until the healing goes to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the wounded limb after surgery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not harm its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that the member should be broken anew, for many foolish people have done this in our land; but such practices are blamed, and they bring great pain and even death. However, if the nodules and torments are fresh, let them be immersed in hot water or soft herbs are boiled, as with leaves of duckweed, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the ointment is made morbifical, as with well-made astringent, and you take musk from duckweed, and confound it with linseed oil or sesamum oil, and make an ointment; or you take fat figs, and grind them with hay of colza, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is the bone moved by constant and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Let there be movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the limb is twisted and hardened, as in stone, it must be opened with iron, covering up to the bone, cutting lightly with a sharp knife; and put on ointment and care in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if he should now bring it back to its place by gentle movement alone.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, and the joints swell up, and by chance does he bring it back to its place by gentle movement when it is swollen: many times this brings about swelling and other pains; nevertheless, when this has happened, you should make the patient well, then leave him, as long as the abscesses are calm; then raise the member with warm water and oil, then move it lightly, and cure each member as the cure comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the ointments for dislocations of the shoulder joint down to the heel.
des mandibules	the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Now let's go over some dislocations of the jaw, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are a little out of place and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the breast, and causing the saliva to flow from the mouth so that he cannot keep it in or close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it with many different positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it in the hospital, and do not tarry at all; and in this way that the minister takes the chief of the illness with his hand on the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are far away, to make it even; and command the patient that he softens his jaws, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the wound remain equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let them be brought back gently, together or separately, if they have been dislocated by cold water and oil, as we have said. Do not hesitate to bring them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they have been brought back equally, and the mouth of the sick person is closed smoothly with a softener, if you put it on drapings wet with oil and wax made of oil and wax, then let it lie gently between them; and let the sick person sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move or strain at all, but relaxes his muscles, as long as the pains are gone and the jaws are healed; and then eat lightly, and do not struggle to open the mouth for food or drink, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour and do not return to their places, then fever and usual heat come, and by chance stomach discharge, and by chance vomit of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times it kills him who has it, in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not come out from inside the body along its extension from the throat and from the mouth, and is dislocated at any time to the side, and we feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies down on his back, and stretches his arms; and then press upon it with your palm, and it will come back; and then put the plaster and bandage on it, and bind it; and if there were no head of shoulder, and if it dislocates at any time, then you bring it back to its place as we have said; then put the plaster and bandage on it, and bind it, and command the patient to rest as long as he is not well; and in this way is the head of the shoulder also brought back.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Here comes the first sentence to translate:
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance came to some men a pounding or break, and swollen the shoulder of an abscess hot, and thought that it was dislocated by him.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It therefore seems that you test it, as far as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it goes down towards the shoulder, and makes a difference between the sick and the healthy shoulder, and you will find between them a great difference; and you will find in the head of the shoulder an abscess, and remove the shoulder to the table the head of the shoulder, as if it were one; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its side, or move at all; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, then it is not hidden, for you can see it clearly on the table; and this kind of dislocation is not worth repairing, when it is new, or when the patient has hurt himself.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the ministers hold the hand of the sick person on high, then put your poultices over the shoulder, and force the joint up to its place; and the ministers hold the hand, and stretch it up, and then they put it away; so come to hospital quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in the hands of a day later, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water; and allow the administrating of softening and soothing infusions, such as an infusion of althaea and fenugrec and mieliette in water, and to be allowed to rest; then let the patient lie on his back, and put a sheet of equal length, not too soft nor too hard, behind the shoulder; and place the minister's hand on the patient's shoulder, and pull down the hand of the sick person; and have another minister rub the patient's chief, so that it does not move downward; this shoulder comes back immediately, and they see if they do so according to this way: and it is that you make present a man who is more powerful than the sick; and let him stand on his right side, and pour out this shoulder behind the shoulder of the sick person, and raise the shoulder up, so that the sick hangs down by his arm; and have other ministers pull down the hand of the sick person towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if you also do it in another way: and is there put a long branch in the earth, whose head is also like a pistol, and not too big or too small; then cover the patient with it, but let it have a drape above it, and the patient lies on the long wood of the branch; then extend his hand towards the other part forming, and the joint will return to its place peacefully; and if it does not return by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a branch of II arms of great and IIII fingers wide, which has the head reont for perfectly enter em in asselle according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie on the head of the branch covered with a drape, so that the wood does not hurt the patient, then put it in the asselle of the patient; and extend your arms over the long branch, and place the shoulder on the branch, and the arm at the head of the hand, and then put the arm over an inch of a stone of great width, and extend the hand towards the other part, and leave the body hanging from one side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is put in place, in any way that is convenient, it is necessary that you put a ball of wool equal, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and olive oil, on all the shoulder and neck, then remove the joint forward, and tie the thread to the plaster, and embrace the hand at the collar, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck a little while, until the members are comfortable, for he will heal more quickly; and then suck again after five or seven days, and move them; and if they are firm and not softened, they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place due to moisture or some other cause, it is necessary that you apply the caustic to three parts, as it is put before or as it is plastered with the caustic.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it sloughs off after seven days, and the joint does not hold fast, and cannot raise his arms up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are either torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never properly set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations near the neck, and behind, are caused by impact, stretching of the hands, and should be treated in another way; and I will instruct you how to do this until they are well.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greasiness to the limb, and tardily moves, then the patient should often bathe, until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation at the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint at the shoulder is dislocated in one direction only, and returns to its place in that same direction; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, then the dislocation is not properly set, for you can see and feel it clearly; and dislocate it according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the bad shoulder with the sound one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder anywhere.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the head of the humerus comes into place, for if the head of the humerus comes into place, it may be reset with great pain; and perhaps it cannot be reset from all sides, especially at the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes great pain, and perhaps leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is possible to do so, when you can, extend his hand with your two hands; and spread his arms wide, and his hands towards the shoulder on the outside, and then bring the joint back to its bone root, or at its base, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is dislocation in front, then return when it doubles its hand to its hand, and fix the root of the palm that has fallen out.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, then give it strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and dye it two ministers, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm of each part, then that you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide; and when you see the joint at the joint to its hand, then oil it with any oil to soften the joint, then tighten the joint correctly, as long as it recovers; and when it is in place, then put it on dry plaster with lamb's blood, and strain it correctly, and wrap the arm around the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, and then undo it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is fixed in its place, and it slides away, and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not fixed well, then begin to plaster and bind it again, and leave it for a few days, until it is firmly set in place; then let it slide.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the reduction of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or put on the joint a wet sheep's wool, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter or bathe; and when it sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the wool back on, and then go in or bathe again; and do this twice or three times, until he is well; and if you see, put on fine sheep's wool heated with butter, and strain it over; then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand should be reset, and it is lighter than other joints However, you must return it to its place as soon as it is dislocated, so that the joint swells or there is an abscess.

And when you reset it, place the bad hand on a table, and extend the fingers, so that the palm faces the joint's edge, and put it back in this position until it heals. However, you must make sure that it is properly aligned; then, place the patient's elbow on a table to extend and reset the arm.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then place the patient' arm on a table, and let the person hold their hand up to the joint' face.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, this is good; but if it does not, then draw out the pus that causes abscesses and leave it in this state without encouraging it to return.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If it cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after some days, then the joint is twisted; do not touch it except to cut off any nerve or artery with a delicate cautery; otherwise, you may only extract it by fire, and perhaps there is no other remedy except to cut it off.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in its place, put the poultice on it that we have described, then draw it out and leave it for 5 days, then remove it and leave it.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, then moisten it with hot water and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not dislocated on either side, nor at the back of the palm or the stomach; so they are, and remove the dislocation to the joints as long as it comes back, then hold the knuckle of the finger with the thumb, and move it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for a day, and then make it equal that day; and from that time on, if it has been dislocated at the base of the hand, and do so often, until it is healthy again; and also do this, when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the shoulder at the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the neck or shoulder is dislocated, or several of them are dislocated, there will be no cure for it, for it kills the patient quickly.

Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens wholesomete, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se mute au derrier si est apelee "gilbositez": li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d'enfance: si n'i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.

And those who come from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment with great words have brought him no great benefit; but I have shortened them according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the giddiness which comes to the back, there is no remedy or cure; and likewise that which comes straight to the II sides, and cannot be cured except by the one who comes to the back, as I say; it is because the patient should lie on his face in an even position, and have a strapping on him so he does not get hurt; then put a fire stick in the ground formed, and another at the feet, and tie a rope between the two stobs, forming a line between the fire and the sick person, and another at the knees, and ankles; and the two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the II sticks; and let them be well tightened, the stick as we have said, and the rope puts his palms on the spine formed, until he revives.

Et s'elle ne revient par ceste cure, si prenne une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l'espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sur l'autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu'il revient au leu; et si tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And if it does not come back with this remedy, then take a tub of three arms long, and chop the side of it, and let the patient lie on his side, and bottle the head of the tub against the side, then put the middle of the tub over the spine; and place the minister's fingers on the other head of the tub, and press firmly until he comes back to his place; and if you see that the fingers slip, then do it with a thumb that returns to the hand.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, put on dried plasters with lots of resin, and then the stitches, and then the stele of a tablet of three inches long, that purple it the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, and the thread of a rope, as we have said, and use the patient subtilely nourishing food until he is well; and if nothing comes at the end of health, then administer softening medicines and soothing with the stele that we have said before; and never once does a piece of lead come on, and never does appearance come in the posterior spine of the back, and think that it is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, for one should not have presumption: perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Here is the translation:
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the hip and shoulder joints come only from dislocations, not like the other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, before and behind, and more inside, and less before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy, it is longer, and more than the healthy genitals, and cannot double the diseased knee at fire; and this is the place that is inflamed and swollen from an abscess, so that the head of the thigh comes in.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of who it comes before, is that this accident is opposite to these in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of who comes before are that their leg is well in accordance with the complement; however, it does not double the knee in pain, and when they want to make them walk, they cannot walk forward, and they hold their urine back, and their ankle swells, and when they go, they go on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip is softened, and the hip bone is out of place at the sides of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And those who have this type of dislocation should be treated if the dislocation is old and does not improve with time, otherwise there will be no cure; and it is better that they do not expect too much.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and tighten it from the inside and outside, and turn it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then it is necessary that you work very hard with one minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it to the ground with a strap around the knee; and let another minister stretch his hand over the joint on both sides, so that he presses his hands together, and then pulls the strap tightly around the hip; and let another minister tie the end of the strap high up and low down at the same time, until the patient is standing straight on the ground for a while, and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is so common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to put the cure on his back at ease, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh, and the one that is out of the hip, then make the bandage go up towards the hip, and towards the force; then press other ministers on their arms, and embrace the large bandage of the diseased thigh, and stretch it to the outside form: now it will come back to its place; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot do it in this way that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two legs of the sick together with a strong rope from one foot to the other, and be more extended than the others; then hang them by the neck on the top of a post, and have two long arms; then order a minister who embraces the head of the thigh, and have other ministers hanging with the sick, who embrace it well, because the joint returns now very easily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	Et when the dislocations are on the side, let the patient lie down, as we have said in that which has gibbosity, and extrude II chains properly upon the sick leg, and also upon the foot; then put II torches, one to the head and one other at the feet, then place I torch between the legs of the patient towards the form; and plant thereof moisten fabrics about, lest he hurt the sick man, then extend each minister toward him, and let him put the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, set him upon a table, and press him thus as we have said in gibbosity, and let the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are before, if it is necessary to extend the sick leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and let him place his pain to be upon the sick ankle, then press with the other hand, and let him extend forward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et si la dislocation est au loin, il ne convient pas de tirer le patient vers l'avant, de le lever sur la terre, mais qu'il soit plutôt placé comme s'il était assis avec les jambes étendues, comme nous l'avons dit plus haut pour le couchage sur les deux hanches; et qu'on le place sur sa face, et que la ligne étendue soit pressée sur la jointure de la table; et elle sera bien lorsque le patient étendra ses jambes, qui seront longues; alors retirez les cuisses, mettez l'ampoule, et l'extraction d'un bandage, de sorte que la hanche ne bouge pas; et qu'il repose trois ou quatre jours, puis que vous le retiriez, et mettez l'ampoule sur; et si vous voyez qu'elles sont longues, tirez-les alors, comme nous l'avons dit, et laissez-les reposer pendant trois jours; puis retirez-les, et faites-le grogner bruyamment, jusqu'à ce que les membres soient confortés.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the hip joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	It is dislocated according to three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient that he bend his leg to his knee, and if he does not flex at his knee, knowing that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put his back on his face, and put his foot on your legs; then take his knee between your hands, and pull apart between your two hands, then bend the II ribs at the knee joint in form; and other ministers extend his foot, until the hip joint returns to its place, and the signs are that he flexes his leg well at his knee leicht; and put the plaster on, and make him raise his leg to the knee, and join them together firmly for III days or IV, then loosen him. And do not work the patient to walk, until the members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, so administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the leg, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never displaced, and never completely dislocated, and in and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and lean before the part where it is dislocated: let us gently ramie, and we must gently extend with our hands when it is only slightly displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the top, so that you make sit the patient upright, and take it by the leg, above the ankle; then bring the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, and then extend it upward, and blow strongly on the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, by blowing and bringing the foot; if it comes back, it is good; if not, begin again the work, for it will come back; and if it does not come back, so make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and put a staff firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie sheets around it, so that he does not move the patient; then take the leg by the ankle, and each minister extends equally, and the staff is held close between the pacient's thighs to hold the patient still while you stretch him; then make the minister who is holding the leg sit upright with his hands, and the other ministers extend the foot at its end, so that he holds the foot firmly above the ankle; then bring the foot back to you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, and then blow strongly on the foot, and do this twice, as we have said, by blowing and bringing the foot; if it comes back, it is good; if not, begin again the work, for it will come back; and if it does not come back, so make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and put a staff firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie sheets around it, so that he does not move the patient; then take the leg by the ankle, and each minister extends equally, and the staff is held close between the pacient's thighs to hold the patient still while you stretch him; then make the minister who is holding the leg sit upright with his hands, and the other ministers extend the foot at its end, so that he holds the foot firmly above the ankle; then bring the foot back to you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, and then blow strongly on the foot, and do this twice, as we have said, by blowing and bringing the foot; if it comes back, it is good; if not, begin again the work, for it will come back; and if it does not come back, so make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and put a staff firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie sheets around it, so that he does not move the patient; then take the leg by the ankle, and each minister extends equally, and the staff is held close between the pacient's thighs to hold the patient still while you stretch him; then make the minister who is holding the leg sit upright with his hands, and the other ministers extend the foot at its end, so that he holds the foot firmly above the ankle;
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set in place, put the plaster on top of it and form it, and fasten the foot to the leg, and ward off the tendons that are behind the ankle, so that the ligatures are not too tight; then let it be for II days or III, and if the strapping has loosened, then release it after a third day, and let the patient go by IV days; and if he goes before this term, it is not yet certain that he will still dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms on the foot, so that you can calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, as long as it is healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so that they can be smoothly extended without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in either of the two feet, so that you can make the patient sit on a plain or  .ie. table all straight, and place your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press upon your foot with form, until it has recovered; and when it is even, and there is no more opening, then strap the sole of the foot to a chair at II joints, then form the strapping, and let it be for III days, then release it; and let it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, unless you are skilled in the art and have used it long ago, and unless you are compassionate and tardy, do not be bold; and use at first soothing things for an abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, now bring the limb back to its place, so that the abscesses come; and when the limbs are in their places, administer drying ointments, and cure the wound, as it should be, with balms; and if there is a fracture with dislocation, and small bones are broken, set the bone, and do what we have said for simple illnesses; and guard against entering the path of fear, according to what I said, because this will cost you much according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
